# Tasks

> The Minsky work queue. Sorted by priority (P0 most urgent → P3 least). The daemon picks the highest-priority unclaimed task with complete rule-9 fields, ships it, opens a draft PR.

## How to read this file

Format: [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md). Each priority section is `## P0` / `## P1` / `## P2` / `## P3`.

Each task is a checkbox line + indented metadata fields. Metadata fields agents read:

| Field | What it does |
|---|---|
| **ID** | Stable kebab-case id; same as the task's branch and PR title |
| **Tags** | Comma-separated, includes priority + topic tags |
| **Milestone** | M1 / M2 / M3 / M4 / M5 (see [MILESTONES.md](MILESTONES.md)); defaults to M1 |
| **Hypothesis** | One-line claim — "doing X causes Y, measured by Z" |
| **Success** | One-line numeric / rubric threshold for shipping |
| **Pivot** | One-line numeric threshold at which the *approach* is abandoned |
| **Measurement** | Exact runnable shell / OTEL / CI command — no English, no `<TBD>` |
| **Anchor** | Real literature citation (Author, Title, Year — Section) |
| **Details** | What to do |
| **Files** | What you'll touch |
| **Acceptance** | Per-criterion checklist for the PR reviewer |
| **Status** | Optional: `shipped` / `in-progress` / `blocked` |
| **Competitive-goal** | Which scorecard metric the task moves (M1.10 lint enforces this on P0/P1) |

**Rule #9 fields are iron** (Hypothesis / Success / Pivot / Measurement / Anchor). The task picker rejects any task missing them. `pnpm exec node novel/cross-repo-runner/dist/index.js` (or `node --input-type=module -e '...pickHostTask...'`) returns `null` for malformed tasks; the daemon silently skips them.

**Claim a task** by appending `(@your-agent-id)` to the task line. **Close a task** by removing its entire block in the same commit that ships it — history lives in `git log`, never mark `[x]`.

## How to pick the next task

1. Read [MILESTONES.md § "Critical path to M1 completion"](MILESTONES.md#critical-path-to-m1-completion). The top item is what's blocking M1.
2. Verify the seven surfaces are aligned (see [AGENTS.md § "15. Milestone alignment gate"](AGENTS.md)). If any is stale, that's your task.
3. Walk P0 → P1 → P2 → P3 in order. Pick the top unclaimed task with all rule-9 fields filled in.
4. Check [DEPRECATED.md](./docs/DEPRECATED.md) before implementing — if the task touches a deprecated feature, use the replacement instead.

<!-- policy: Optional `**Status**:` field with allowed values `shipped`, `in-progress`, `blocked`. Consumed by `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion` (P0 watchdog filed in #346): explicit `shipped` + at least one merged PR named after the task ID is the operator-controlled fast path for auto-removal; `in-progress` or `blocked` vetoes auto-removal regardless of merged PRs. Absent field falls back to heuristics (acceptance-checkboxes + merged-PR title match). Format-agnostic — works identically for single-file `TASKS.md` and per-task `tasks/<id>.md` once that migration ships (filed as P2 follow-up of `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion`). -->
<!-- policy: Investor / product-manager / growth-analyst personas only run when **Tags** contains business, growth, revenue, customer, or pricing. -->
<!-- policy: Every term used here must appear in vision.md § Glossary or be sourced from a cited paper. New jargon → glossary entry in the same commit. -->
<!-- policy: Per constitutional rule #9 (pre-registered hypothesis-driven development — iron rule), every new task entry MUST include — in addition to the existing Details / Files / Verification / Acceptance / Risk fields — a runnable Measurement command (shell / OTEL query / CI script that produces the metric) and an explicit Pivot threshold (the value below which the *approach* is abandoned, not just the change reverted). The rule is iron: no exemption for bugfixes, refactors, or "small" fixes — a bugfix declares the stability metric (error rate, recurrence count, MTTR, etc.) it expects to move and by how much. If the metric source doesn't exist yet, ship a preparation PR first that lands the instrumentation. Vanity metrics (counts that always go up — LOC, commits, hours, tasks-in-flight) and post-hoc metrics (chosen after the result) are forbidden. Existing tasks predating rule #9 are retrofitted under task `rule-9-backfill-existing-tasks`. -->
<!-- policy: Per constitutional rule #8 (pattern conformance), every new top-level artifact (file under novel/ or distribution/, root-level *.md, novel pnpm workspace package) requires a row in vision.md § Pattern conformance index in the same commit. -->
<!-- policy: Per constitutional rule #7 (chaos engineering), every new novel package's README and every new user-story includes a "Failure modes & chaos verification" section with steady-state hypothesis, blast radius, operator escape hatch, and a failure-mode table (failure mode | trigger / fault axis | expected behavior — loud-crash-supervisor-restart / circuit-break-and-notify / graceful-degrade | chaos test). -->
<!-- policy: Every task should carry a **Milestone**: M1/M2/M3/M4/M5 field (see MILESTONES.md). Tasks without a milestone field default to M1. M1 = Stable + Measurable + One-Command; M2 = Fast Mode single-task delivery; M3 = GitHub Actions free CI; M4 = Enterprise Reliability 99.9%; M5 = Managed Product. -->
<!-- policy: MILESTONE ALIGNMENT GATE (supersedes all other policies). Before picking ANY implementation task, the agent MUST verify that the following 7 surfaces are up-to-date and aligned with the current milestone in MILESTONES.md: (1) README.md — reflects current milestone's install/run/benefits; (2) Quickstart in README — matches the actual one-command flow for the current milestone; (3) vision.md — milestone goals are reflected in success criteria; (4) user-stories/ — each milestone exit criterion has a corresponding user story with metric + integration test; (5) Integration tests — user-story tests exist and pass for the current milestone's shipped criteria; (6) Logs + observability — OTEL spans, daemon logs, and orchestrate.jsonl capture the data needed to verify the current milestone's exit criteria; (7) METRICS.md — every metric the current milestone depends on has a real observation (not a stub). If ANY of these 7 surfaces is stale or misaligned, the agent's FIRST task is to update them — not to pick an implementation task. This is operator directive 2026-05-18 and is iron: no exemption. Run `node scripts/check-milestone-alignment.mjs` (when it exists) or manually audit the 7 surfaces. -->

## P0

<!-- Operator directive 2026-05-18 (ABSOLUTE PRIORITY — supersedes ALL other P0s including self-metrics-competitive-benchmark): the milestone-alignment-gate task below must be picked FIRST by any agent. No implementation task may be claimed until the 7 surfaces are verified aligned. This is the pre-condition for all other work. -->

<!-- Operator directive 2026-05-27 (UI = P0-P1 by definition): every user-facing CLI surface (bin/minsky subcommands, pnpm minsky:* scripts) defaults to P0-P1 priority — never P2-P3. UX friction compounds: a flag operators have to remember on every debugging session is a 5-second tax × N sessions × M operators = real wasted hours. Backfill any UI task currently at P2-P3 to P1 unless explicitly deferred with a written reason. -->

<!-- 8h-run observability suite (operator directive 2026-06-03):           -->
<!-- prerequisites for the "minsky on itself" 8h soak run. The goal is     -->
<!-- concrete, VISIBLE, browser-verified, externally-reported run metrics: -->
<!-- uptime · tasks/run · cost/task · errors · speed · quality · vs-       -->
<!-- competitors. Each task reuses existing substrate (METRICS.md,         -->
<!-- collect-metrics.mjs, the ledgers, token-monitor + observability       -->
<!-- adapters, competitive-benchmark) — do NOT reinvent. Land these before -->
<!-- the run so the run can also pick them up. All are documented in       -->
<!-- docs/observability-8h-run.md and verified via agent-browser.          -->

- [ ] `obs-run-session-ledger` — give every supervised run ONE consolidated log + a `run-summary.json` (uptime, restarts, throughput), so an 8h run is one readable record instead of scattered JSONL
  - **ID**: obs-run-session-ledger
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, stability, run-metrics, milestone-m1
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs`, `scripts/run-summary.test.mjs`, `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: feeds `daemon-stability-pct` + `deploy-frequency` — without a per-run uptime/throughput record, Minsky's own scorecard column stays empty.
  - **Hypothesis**: a run's evidence is scattered across `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl`, `experiment-store/*.jsonl`, `.minsky/failures/`, and raw `.out/.err` logs, so "how long did it run uninterrupted and how many tasks shipped?" needs manual jq across ≥4 sources. A single `.minsky/runs/<run-id>/` (consolidated `run.log` + `run-summary.json`) makes both answerable with one command.
  - **Success**: after a run, `.minsky/runs/<run-id>/run-summary.json` contains `{ runId, startedAt, endedAt, totalUptimeSec, longestUninterruptedSec, restartCount, tasksAttempted, tasksMerged }`, all derived from existing ledgers; `run.log` interleaves orchestrate + tick-loop + failure events in timestamp order.
  - **Pivot**: if a faithful consolidated log can't be derived from append-only ledgers (interleave races, missing ts), emit `run-summary.json` only and have the dashboard link the source ledgers — do NOT maintain a second write path that can drift from the ledgers.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/run-summary.mjs --run latest --json | jq -e '.longestUninterruptedSec >= 0 and .tasksMerged >= 0 and (.runId|length>0)'` exits 0 after a run.
  - **Anchor**: Avizienis, Laprie, Randell, Landwehr, "Basic Concepts and Taxonomy of Dependable and Secure Computing", IEEE TDSC 2004 (continuity/uptime as a dependability attribute); rule #4 (metrics must be visible).
  - **Details**: Reuse existing data — no parallel hot-loop instrumentation. `scripts/run-summary.mjs` reads `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` (tick ts, workerAlive, healed, merged[]), `.minsky/runany-restart-state.json` (restartIndex, originMs), and `experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl` (verdicts) for the active run, then writes `run-summary.json` + a ts-ordered `run.log`. Longest-uninterrupted = max span between consecutive restart/`healed:true` events. Throughput = count of merged PRs.
  - **Files**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs` (new), `scripts/run-summary.test.mjs` (new), `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (stamp run-id at run start), `docs/observability-8h-run.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (a) schema as in Success, derived purely from existing ledgers; (b) deterministic unit test over fixture ledgers (known input → known uptime/throughput); (c) surfaced on the dashboard (`obs-browser-verified-run-dashboard`) and agent-browser-verified; (d) documented in `docs/observability-8h-run.md`; (e) graceful-degrade: missing ledger → field `null`, never a crash.

- [ ] `obs-error-capture-and-reporter` — capture the FULL list of errors a run hits (untruncated, classified) and report them off-box via a swappable `ErrorReporter` adapter (Sentry + local-file strategies)
  - **ID**: obs-error-capture-and-reporter
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, errors, sentry, adapter, stability, milestone-m1
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `novel/adapters/error-reporter/**`, `scripts/export-run-errors.mjs`, `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `scripts/capture-failure.sh`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: feeds `change-fail-rate` / `regression-escape-rate` — an error budget is uncomputable without a complete, classified error ledger.
  - **Hypothesis**: caught errors are truncated today (orchestrate.jsonl `sweepError` ≤200 chars, experiment-store notes ≤100 chars) and `.minsky/failures/` is ring-limited to 20, so a long run silently loses error detail and nothing leaves the box. A full `errors.jsonl` (untruncated text + class + exit code + duration) plus an `ErrorReporter` adapter shipping each error to Sentry means zero detail lost and errors visible off-box.
  - **Success**: every caught error appends one full row to `.minsky/runs/<run-id>/errors.jsonl` `{ ts, runId, taskId, class, message, stack?, exitCode?, durationMs? }`; an `ErrorReporter` adapter (`novel/adapters/error-reporter/`) with `SentryErrorReporter` + `FileErrorReporter` strategies is wired into the orchestrate tick catch and `capture-failure.sh`; `count(errors.jsonl) == count(reporter sink events)`.
  - **Pivot**: if hosted Sentry is unavailable or conflicts with the local-first preference, default the adapter to a self-hostable strategy (GlitchTip / OpenObserve OTLP / `FileErrorReporter`) — the interface is the deliverable, the SaaS is swappable; never hard-couple the hot loop to one vendor.
  - **Measurement**: `node novel/adapters/error-reporter/dist/selftest.js` exits 0, and `node scripts/export-run-errors.mjs --run latest --json | jq 'length'` equals `jq 'length' .minsky/runs/<id>/errors-reported.jsonl` (FileErrorReporter sink).
  - **Anchor**: Majors, Fong-Jones, Miranda, "Observability Engineering", O'Reilly 2022 (high-cardinality error events); rule #2 (every external dependency behind an adapter interface).
  - **Details**: New `novel/adapters/error-reporter/` with `interface ErrorReporter { report(err, ctx): Promise<void>; selfTest() }`, a `SentryErrorReporter` (wraps `@sentry/node captureException`), and a `FileErrorReporter` (appends `errors-reported.jsonl`) as the offline default. Wire into `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` tick catch and `capture-failure.sh`. Classify errors (spawn-failed / lint-failed / timeout / gate-failed / crash). No secrets in payloads (reuse `check-otel-no-pii` discipline).
  - **Files**: `novel/adapters/error-reporter/src/{index,sentry,file,selftest}.ts` (new), `scripts/export-run-errors.mjs` (new), `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `scripts/capture-failure.sh`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (a) interface + 2 strategies + selfTest; (b) full untruncated classified `errors.jsonl`; (c) wired into tick + capture-failure; (d) no-PII lint passes on payloads; (e) errors visible in the external sink AND on the dashboard, agent-browser-verified; (f) documented; (g) graceful-degrade: a reporter failure never crashes the run (rule #6 — log locally, continue).

- [ ] `obs-cost-and-latency-per-task` — measure cost-per-task (USD/tokens) and per-task speed (latency) live, by joining the existing token-monitor adapter with ledger timestamps
  - **ID**: obs-cost-and-latency-per-task
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, cost, latency, run-metrics, milestone-m1
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs`, `novel/adapters/token-monitor/src/index.ts`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: fills `cost-per-merged-pr` + `mean-autonomous-merge-latency` — the two metrics most quoted against Devin/OpenHands.
  - **Hypothesis**: `tokens-per-story` and `mttr` are STUBs ("no OTEL backend"), yet the data exists — MaciekTokenMonitor reads per-session token usage and the ledgers carry per-iteration timestamps. Joining them per task makes cost-per-task and latency real numbers.
  - **Success**: `run-summary.json` gains `perTask: [{ taskId, costUsd, tokensIn, tokensOut, latencySec }]` plus roll-ups `meanCostPerMergedPr` + `meanMergeLatencySec`, derived from token-monitor snapshots + ledger ts (no new hot-loop calls).
  - **Pivot**: if per-task token attribution is ambiguous (a session spans multiple tasks), amortize session cost across that session's merged tasks and LABEL it `costAttribution: "amortized"` — never report false-precision per-task cost.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/run-summary.mjs --run latest --json | jq -e '.meanCostPerMergedPr >= 0 and .meanMergeLatencySec >= 0'` exits 0.
  - **Anchor**: Kohavi, Tang, Xu, "Trustworthy Online Controlled Experiments", Cambridge 2020 (cost/latency as first-class metrics); rule #4.
  - **Details**: Extend `scripts/run-summary.mjs` (from `obs-run-session-ledger`) to read `novel/adapters/token-monitor` snapshots and join on the task window. Cost in USD via the model's published per-token price (config, not hardcoded). Latency = `merged_ts − task_pick_ts` from the ledger.
  - **Files**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs`, `novel/adapters/token-monitor/src/index.ts` (expose per-window usage if needed), `docs/observability-8h-run.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (a) perTask cost+latency + roll-ups; (b) attribution method labeled; (c) dashboard tiles + agent-browser verification; (d) documented; (e) deterministic test over a fixture session+ledger pair.

- [ ] `obs-result-quality-score` — attach a result-quality score to each merged task so the run reports quality, not just quantity
  - **ID**: obs-result-quality-score
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, quality, run-metrics, milestone-m1
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: feeds `gate-pass-rate` + `change-fail-rate` — quality is the axis competitors compete on, currently a `—` in Minsky's column.
  - **Hypothesis**: current run signals are structural (files changed, CI green) and don't answer "was the work good?". A composite quality score per merged task (first-push CI green × PR self-grade × tests-added × no same-day revert) yields one comparable quality number.
  - **Success**: `run-summary.json` `perTask[].quality` ∈ [0,1] from those components, plus roll-up `meanQuality`; component breakdown stored alongside.
  - **Pivot**: if a component needs human input, ship the objective sub-score (CI-green × tests-added × no-revert) and mark the review component `null` — partial-but-honest beats unmeasured.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/run-summary.mjs --run latest --json | jq -e '.meanQuality >= 0 and .meanQuality <= 1'` exits 0.
  - **Anchor**: Forsgren, Humble, Kim, "Accelerate", 2018 (change-fail-rate / quality as a delivery metric, not a vanity count); rule #4.
  - **Details**: Extend `run-summary.mjs`. Reuse the existing `pr-self-grade` lint output and `spec-alignment` CI data; detect tests-added from the diff; detect reverts from git log. Composite weights documented + configurable.
  - **Files**: `scripts/run-summary.mjs`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (a) perTask.quality + meanQuality + component breakdown; (b) dashboard tile + agent-browser verification; (c) documented; (d) deterministic test over fixtures.

- [ ] `obs-live-competitive-self-column` — restore the deleted live-ingest pipeline so Minsky's OWN run metrics appear as a scorecard column, head-to-head with competitors
  - **ID**: obs-live-competitive-self-column
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, competitive, scorecard, milestone-m1, m1-10
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `novel/competitive-benchmark/src/**`, `scripts/benchmark-run.mjs`, `scripts/render-scorecard-md.mjs`, `competitors/scorecard.md`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: this IS the competitive surface — it places Minsky's `autonomous-merge-rate`, `cost-per-merged-pr`, `mean-autonomous-merge-latency`, `human-intervention-rate`, `daemon-stability-pct` against every competitor in `competitors.ts`.
  - **Hypothesis**: the scorecard's Minsky column is all `—` because the live-ingest pipeline (`benchmark-run.mjs` / `computeMinskyReadings` / `bin/minsky competitive`) was deleted in the 2026-05-28 Path-A cut. Re-deriving Minsky's readings from `run-summary.json` and rendering a Minsky column makes "Minsky vs competitor X" a real comparison on ≥5 shared metrics.
  - **Success**: `node scripts/benchmark-run.mjs --run latest` writes `.minsky/competitive-scorecard.json` with a `minsky` entry sourced from `run-summary.json`; regenerated `competitors/scorecard.md` shows ≥5 Minsky cells filled with a delta vs each competitor sharing that metric.
  - **Pivot**: if a run is too short for a stable reading (n<5 merged PRs for a metric), render that cell as `(n too small)` rather than a misleading point estimate — honesty over a vanity number (rule #4).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/benchmark-run.mjs --run latest --json | jq -e '[.minsky.values | to_entries[] | select(.value != null)] | length >= 5'` exits 0.
  - **Anchor**: Basili, Caldiera, Rombach, "The Goal-Question-Metric Approach", 1994 (compare against a baseline on the same operationalized metric); prior plan `docs/plans/self-metrics-competitive-benchmark.md` (slice c).
  - **Details**: Re-implement the deleted reducer behind the existing `metrics.ts` catalogue: read `run-summary.json`, map to the 5 ledger-derivable metric ids, call `computeDelta()` vs each competitor's published values, emit the scorecard JSON, regenerate `competitors/scorecard.md`. Competitors stay pure data (rule #2).
  - **Files**: `novel/competitive-benchmark/src/{ledger,scorecard}.ts` (re-add), `scripts/benchmark-run.mjs` (re-add), `scripts/render-scorecard-md.mjs`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (a) Minsky self-column with ≥5 filled metrics + deltas; (b) small-n honesty guard; (c) scorecard rendered + agent-browser-verified on the dashboard; (d) documented; (e) competitors stay pure data; (f) deterministic test over a fixture `run-summary.json`.

- [ ] `obs-browser-verified-run-dashboard` — ONE live dashboard page showing the run's metrics + competitive comparison, gated by an agent-browser smoke test, plus the umbrella runbook
  - **ID**: obs-browser-verified-run-dashboard
  - **Tags**: p0, observability, dashboard, ui, browser-verified, docs, milestone-m1
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Touches**: `novel/dashboard-web/src/**`, `scripts/verify-dashboard-browser.mjs`, `docs/observability-8h-run.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: surfaces every other obs metric (uptime, throughput, cost/task, latency, errors, quality, competitive deltas) in one glanceable place — rule #4 visibility made real.
  - **Hypothesis**: the metrics above are useless if no one can see them at a glance. A single dashboard route rendering `run-summary.json` + the competitive scorecard, proven to render by an agent-browser smoke test, lets an operator (and a reviewer) verify the 8h run's health in one screen.
  - **Success**: a route (e.g. `/run` on the existing dashboard-web server) renders tiles for uptime, tasks-merged, cost/task, mean latency, error count, mean quality, and the Minsky-vs-competitor table; an agent-browser script opens it and asserts each tile shows a value.
  - **Pivot**: if reviving the deprecated `dashboard-web` SSR is too unstable, render a static `.minsky/runs/<id>/report.html` from `run-summary.json` and agent-browser-verify THAT — a stable static artifact beats a flaky live server (rule #6/#7).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/verify-dashboard-browser.mjs` (drives agent-browser, asserts the 7 tiles are present + non-empty) exits 0.
  - **Anchor**: Card, Mackinlay, Shneiderman, "Readings in Information Visualization", 1999 (glanceable, overview-first display); rule #4 (visible metrics) + rule #7 (graceful degrade).
  - **Details**: Extend `novel/dashboard-web` (or the static-report fallback) to read `run-summary.json` + `.minsky/competitive-scorecard.json`. Add `scripts/verify-dashboard-browser.mjs` using the `agent-browser` skill to open the page and assert tiles. Write `docs/observability-8h-run.md` as the single runbook: what each metric means, where it is stored, the exact command to view it, and the copy-paste agent-browser verification command.
  - **Files**: `novel/dashboard-web/src/{server,render}.ts`, `scripts/verify-dashboard-browser.mjs` (new), `docs/observability-8h-run.md` (new — umbrella runbook for the whole suite).
  - **Acceptance**: (a) one page with all 7 tiles + competitive table; (b) agent-browser smoke test asserts tiles non-empty and IS the merge gate; (c) `docs/observability-8h-run.md` documents every metric, its storage, view command, and the browser-verification command; (d) graceful-degrade: a missing metric shows `—`, page still renders; (e) the runbook's agent-browser command is copy-pasteable and verified.

- [ ] `local-gate-merge-test-anti-flake` — make `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs` deterministic under host-oversubscription. During parallel delivery waves (many worktree agents at once) its subprocess-heavy cases time out and red the worker's `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full`, causing agents to spuriously self-mark tasks blocked even though CI (a single un-oversubscribed job) passes the same test. Multiple 2026-06 grind agents hit this.
  - **ID**: local-gate-merge-test-anti-flake
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, stability, anti-flake, flake-guard, test-determinism
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: protects autonomous-delivery throughput — a flaky gate that spuriously blocks tractable tasks is a direct hit to merge-rate, the M1 differentiator vs Devin/OpenHands.
  - **Hypothesis**: the timeouts come from unbounded/short per-subprocess waits in `local-gate-merge.test.mjs` that assume an unloaded host; bounding each spawned step with a generous, explicit timeout (and/or serializing the heaviest cases with `describe.sequential`) makes the suite pass under ≥3x CPU oversubscription, dropping spurious-block events from observed (≥1/parallel-wave) to 0.
  - **Success**: running the suite under simulated load — `for i in 1 2 3 4 5 6; do (pnpm vitest run scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs &); done; wait` — all six concurrent runs exit 0; and a single `pnpm vitest run scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs` exits 0 in <60s.
  - **Pivot**: if bounding timeouts + sequential isolation still flake under 6x load, mark the host-spawning cases `it.skipIf(process.env.MINSKY_CI_LIGHT)` and run them only in the single-job CI lane, abandoning the under-load guarantee for the worktree lane.
  - **Measurement**: `for i in 1 2 3 4 5 6; do pnpm vitest run scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs >/tmp/lgm-$i.log 2>&1 & done; wait; grep -L "failed" /tmp/lgm-*.log | wc -l | grep -qx 6 && echo PASS`
  - **Anchor**: Fowler, M., "Eradicating Non-Determinism in Tests", martinfowler.com 2011 (resource-contention flakes); Meszaros, *xUnit Test Patterns*, 2007 § "Slow Tests" (bound external-process waits).
  - **Details**: audit `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs` for `spawnSync`/`execSync`/vitest-default-timeout cases; give each an explicit generous `{ timeout }` and wrap the merge-clone heavy cases in `describe.sequential` so they don't contend with each other under wave-parallel load. Keep the assertions identical.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs`
  - **Touches**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs`
  - **Acceptance**: six concurrent suite runs all exit 0; single run <60s; assertions unchanged; `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.

- [ ] `mcp-migration-to-2026-07-28-rc` — migrate Minsky's MCP adapter to the v2026-07-28 RC protocol revision before the breaking-change deadline. v2026-07-28 removes the `initialize` handshake and moves MCP to stateless semantics; without the migration, Minsky's MCP adapter breaks against any post-July-28 MCP server.
  - **ID**: mcp-migration-to-2026-07-28-rc
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m1, mcp, protocol-migration, time-bounded-deadline-2026-07-28, operator-directive-2026-05-28
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: drives `mcp-protocol-version-currency` (new metric — fraction of MCP traffic on the current stable protocol revision). Without this migration, Minsky's MCP adapter becomes incompatible with any MCP server running the new protocol after July 28, 2026 — every companion-mode agentbrew skill that updates its MCP server fails Minsky's adapter.
  - **Hypothesis**: re-implementing the version-specific transport layer at `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts` (sibling to the current `mcp.v2025-11-25.ts`) and switching the canonical implementation pointer in `novel/adapters/mcp.openhands.ts` is a self-contained ~1-week change. The adapter's 3-verb interface stays stable; only the JSON-RPC envelope structure changes (stateless vs session-based, no `initialize` handshake).
  - **Success**: (1) `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts` ships with full coverage of the v2025-11-25 verb set against v2026-07-28 semantics. (2) The adapter integration test runs against BOTH protocol versions (paired-fixture pattern). (3) The cutover happens at least 7 days before the July 28, 2026 deadline (gives buffer for any post-cutover regression). (4) No consumer of `novel/adapters/mcp.ts` (the interface) requires modification — the interface is stable across the migration.
  - **Pivot**: if v2026-07-28 RC ships with unannounced additional breaking changes (e.g., a new resource semantics that doesn't map 1:1 to v2025-11-25), the migration becomes a 2-week project and we ship a `version=2025-11-25` fallback flag in the adapter so operators with stale MCP servers can opt out for one more cycle. Abandon the migration only if Anthropic delays the v2026-07-28 release by ≥6 months.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/adapters/mcp/test/ --reporter=verbose -t v2026-07-28` exits 0; the existing v2025-11-25 tests continue to pass (paired-fixture protocol-version-matrix lint).
  - **Anchor**: `docs/research-a2a-mcp-2026-05-28.md` § "MCP v2025-11-25 — Model Context Protocol" (the migration note); MCP v2026-07-28 RC release notes at <https://modelcontextprotocol.io/changelog> (when published); SEP-2575 (the spec proposal that removes the initialize handshake).
  - **Details**: Single-slice. (1) Write `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts` as a sibling of the v2025-11-25 implementation. (2) Add a `protocol_version` parameter to `novel/adapters/mcp.openhands.ts` that selects between the two transport layers. (3) Update the integration test to run the same 8 paired cases against BOTH protocol versions. (4) Once Anthropic publishes the v2026-07-28 GA, flip the default to the new version + open a follow-up to delete the v2025-11-25 transport in ~3 months.
  - **Files**: `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts` (new), `novel/adapters/mcp.openhands.ts` (update — protocol_version param), `test/integration/mcp-adapter-fixture.test.ts` (update — paired tests across versions), `docs/research-a2a-mcp-2026-05-28.md` (add a "migration completed YYYY-MM-DD" footer when done).
  - **Touches**: `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts`, `novel/adapters/mcp.openhands.ts`, `test/integration/mcp-adapter-fixture.test.ts`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `novel/adapters/mcp.v2026-07-28.ts` exists with the full verb-set transport. (2) The integration test runs across both protocol versions with all paired cases passing. (3) The cutover lands by **2026-07-21** (7 days of buffer before the July 28 deadline). (4) The `novel/adapters/mcp.ts` interface is unchanged (zero consumer-side updates). (5) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.
  - **Risk**: low. The MCP team has been transparent about the breaking-change shape (per the public SEP-2575); the migration is a known quantity. The only material risk is the v2026-07-28 RC slipping or shipping with surprise additional breaks — covered in the Pivot.
  - **Composes-with**: `mcp-adapter-foundation` (the prerequisite that this migrates).
  - **Blocked**: needs `mcp-adapter-foundation` to ship first.

- [ ] `no-useful-work-class-operator-decision` — qwen3-coder:30b on OpenHands SDK reliably engages with the brief (reads it, runs one tool call) but emits prose-only replies after the first turn, triggering the SDK's conversation-end signal with files_changed=0. The brief-reorder PR #978 reduced the failure surface (input tokens 90K→70K, iteration time 130s→79s) but the residual is a MODEL TOOL-CALLING RELIABILITY limit, not a brief-structure issue. Closing the class requires an operator choice between three paths.
  - **ID**: no-useful-work-class-operator-decision
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Operator-owned decision (A/B/C); needs live daemon data + 24h post-choice window, absent.
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, stability, local-llm, model-choice, agent-framework, operator-decision-required, observed-2026-05-28
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: drives `local-models-default-clean-exit-fraction` (M1.5 stability target, user-story 015) toward ≥60% — currently ~20% (operator observed 5/5 last iterations no-progress). Without this, the M1.1 stability gate cannot lift and `cloud_agent: "openhands"` stays the default forever, defeating user-story 015's "local models until we're super stable" stance.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-28 operator session — 5 PRs delivered the cold-spawn crash class, picker-blocked-because alias, TASKS.md hygiene sweep, and brief-reorder. After all four, the supervisor still showed `verdict: no-progress` on `agent-mediated-install` and `minsky-human-comm-via-file` because the local model emits prose like "Now let me check the bin directory to see what's there currently:" without an attached tool call. OpenHands SDK terminates the conversation. `files_changed=0`, `pr_url=null`. Diagnostic at `.minsky/failures/2026-05-28T142223Z-agent-mediated-install/stdout.log` confirms the pattern.
  - **Hypothesis**: closing this class requires operator-selectable mitigation from this menu (rank ordered by expected ROI):
    - **(A) Bigger local model** — switch `~/.minsky/config.json` `cloud_agent_model` from `ollama_chat/qwen3-coder:30b` to `ollama_chat/qwen3-coder:480b` OR `mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit` (Opus-quality dense, per `worker-model-per-machine-config` task). The 30B floor was always provisional; the diagnose self-fix log explicitly recommends this when no-progress rate stays high.
    - **(B) Different agent framework** — wire aider as an alternative local agent. `~/.minsky/config.json` already documents `local_agent: "aider"` but `scripts/spawn_agent.py` only dispatches to OpenHands. Aider takes `--message-file` (different brief shape) and edits files directly without OpenHands' tool-call-or-die semantics. Estimated work: ~2-3h (new `scripts/spawn_aider.py` shim + dispatcher branching + integration test).
    - **(C) Accept the trade-off** — keep cloud Claude as the runtime path for any task that needs autonomous coding; demote local-LLM to "best-effort overnight" mode. Documented in `~/.minsky/config.json` doc + `user-stories/015` follow-up; the stance from 2026-05-24 ("local models until we're super stable") softens to "local models for non-shipping work; cloud for the deliverable path".
  - **Success**: operator picks one of (A) / (B) / (C) and either: ships the implementation (if A or B) or documents the trade-off (if C). The `daemon-no-progress-rate` self-diagnose finding shrinks from 5/5 to <2/5 over a 24h window post-decision.
  - **Pivot**: if (A) — operator bumps the model and observes no improvement in the no-progress-rate, fall back to (B). If (B) — aider wiring lands and the same no-progress class shows up against aider, the residual is genuinely the local-LLM tier (rule #15 milestone-alignment gate fires and (C) becomes the only remaining option).
  - **Measurement**: `cat .minsky/iterations.jsonl | jq 'select(.verdict == "no-progress") | .ts' | sort | uniq -c` over the trailing 24h window; targeted iteration count <2 out of 5.
  - **Anchor**: `user-stories/015-local-models-until-stable.md` § "Failure modes" — the "Stability stays below 60% long-term (local models are *worse*, not the same)" row explicitly says "rule #15 milestone-alignment gate fires; the operator must decide whether to keep the stance"; PR #978's hypothesis self-grade documented "Match: partial" because front-loading the discipline reduced but did not close the class.
  - **Details**: This is a triage / operator-decision task, not a code task. The agent picking this should: (a) read `.minsky/failures/<latest>/stdout.log` to confirm the disengagement pattern is still active; (b) read `.minsky/iterations.jsonl` to compute the rolling no-progress-rate; (c) surface the three options above to the operator with concrete numbers; (d) when the operator picks A or B, the agent files a CHILD task implementing the choice. The agent does NOT pick the option itself — this is a strategic trade-off (cost vs. capability) that's explicitly operator-owned per user-story 015's stance.
  - **Files**: docs/validated-learnings.md (record the operator's decision + rationale), TASKS.md (file the child implementation task), `~/.minsky/config.json` (if A — operator-side edit, not code).
  - **Touches**: docs/validated-learnings.md, TASKS.md, user-stories/015-local-models-until-stable.md
  - **Acceptance**: (1) Operator's choice (A / B / C) is captured in `docs/validated-learnings.md` with a dated entry. (2) If A: `~/.minsky/config.json` reflects the new model + ≥1 iteration against the new model has `files_changed > 0`. If B: aider dispatch ships as a child PR + ≥1 iteration via aider has `files_changed > 0`. If C: `user-stories/015` is updated to reflect the softened stance + the M1.1 stability gate's local-models criterion is dropped/replaced. (3) The `daemon-no-progress-rate` self-diagnose finding under `.minsky/findings/` shows the rolling rate <40% within 24h of the choice landing.
  - **Risk**: low. This is a clarifying task that asks for the operator's decision; the risk is the operator deferring indefinitely. Mitigation: this task's `**Milestone**: M1` flagging means the milestone-alignment gate (rule #15) will fire if it stays unblocked too long, surfacing it on every PR review.
  - **Note**: composes with `worker-model-per-machine-config` (existing P0 task — "pin this Mac to mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit") which is option (A)'s concrete implementation surface, and with the existing `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` (P0) which proposes opencode as an alternative local stack (a variant of option B).

- [ ] `minsky-npm-publish-v0-1-0` — operator-step: publish the first release of the `minsky` npm package so `npx minsky init` works for any operator on any machine. The publishable substrate (package.json bin + files, regression test, smoke test) shipped in PR (this PR) — what's left is the credentials-gated push to npmjs.com
  - **ID**: minsky-npm-publish-v0-1-0
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, m1-3, operator-step, install, distribution, blocked-needs-operator
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: drives `install-success-rate` (M1.3) toward "1 on fresh machine without git clone" — Devin / Cline / Aider all distribute via package managers (pip / vscode marketplace / brew). Minsky's `git clone + pnpm install` flow is the high outlier today; `npx -y minsky init` closes the gap.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-26 operator session on M1.3 substrate completion. The tarball builds + bin/minsky init runs end-to-end from the unpacked tarball (verified via `pnpm vitest run test/integration/npx-init-tarball.test.ts`). The remaining gap is exactly the credential-gated npmjs.com push.
  - **Hypothesis**: a single `npm publish` from a CI environment with NPM_TOKEN secret (or operator's machine with `npm login`) at the `v0.1.0` git tag publishes the `minsky` package to npmjs.com. Once live, any operator on any machine runs `npx -y minsky init` → `minsky` and the daemon starts within 60s.
  - **Success**: (1) `npm view minsky version` returns ≥`0.1.0` on npmjs.com. (2) `npx -y minsky --version` on a fresh `node:24-bookworm` Docker container prints the package version without errors. (3) `npx -y minsky init` writes `~/.minsky/config.json` correctly. (4) `npm view minsky size` returns ≤5 MB compressed (npm convention).
  - **Pivot**: if the `minsky` name is unexpectedly taken on npmjs.com (it wasn't as of 2026-05-26 — `curl https://registry.npmjs.org/minsky` returned 404), publish as `@fyodoriv/minsky` instead and document `npx -y @fyodoriv/minsky init` as the canonical command. Operator updates README + the launchpad lines.
  - **Measurement**: `curl -fsSL https://registry.npmjs.org/minsky 2>/dev/null | jq -r '.["dist-tags"].latest'` returns a non-null version string OR the equivalent for the pivot namespace.
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (npm is the universal Node distribution channel — don't reinvent); `user-stories/006-runner-on-any-repo.md` § Acceptance criterion §3 (one-command install); Krug *Don't Make Me Think* 2014 (one obvious path).
  - **Details**: (a) Operator runs `npm login` (or sets `NPM_TOKEN` in GitHub Actions secrets); (b) verifies the package.json shape one more time (`bin`, `files`, version, license, repository, keywords); (c) tags the release (`git tag v0.1.0 && git push origin v0.1.0`); (d) runs `pnpm publish --access=public --no-git-checks` (the operator's machine; CI publishing is a follow-up); (e) smokes the result via `npx -y minsky --version` in a fresh Docker container.
  - **Files**: `package.json` (bump version from `0.1.0-rc.0` → `0.1.0`), `README.md` (drop "release-candidate" language once live).
  - **Touches**: package.json, README.md
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `npx -y minsky --version` on a fresh machine prints the published version. (2) `npm view minsky` shows ≥0.1.0 and a tarball size ≤5MB. (3) the integration test `test/integration/npx-init-tarball.test.ts` continues to pass against the local tarball (the regression site for any future package.json regression).
  - **Risk**: low. The publication is one shell command; the risk is forgetting to bump version BEFORE publish (publishing `0.1.0-rc.0` instead of `0.1.0`) or publishing with the wrong namespace. Mitigation: the integration test asserts `package.json.version` matches the bump pattern; the operator's checklist is the npm-publish skill in their dotfiles.
  - **Blocked**: blocked-needs-operator-credentials — the actual `npm publish` requires npm credentials the daemon can't access. Operator-only step.
  - **Note**: composes with the previously-filed `minsky-npx-install-and-run` (P1) for the FULL `npx minsky` (no subcommand) flow — once `init` works, the next step is the `npx minsky` (no subcommand) detect-and-init-then-start path. This task ships the `init` half; the `minsky-npx-install-and-run` task ships the integrated `npx minsky` flow on top.

- [ ] `add-openhands-as-pluggable-backend` — add `openhands` as a 4th pluggable agent in `~/.minsky/config.json` (alongside `claude` / `devin` / `aider`) to inherit its 65.8% SWE-bench-verified single-task agent
  - **ID**: add-openhands-as-pluggable-backend
  - **Tags**: p0, external-dep-blocked, wrap-feasibility, openhands, agent-backend, observed-2026-05-22, approved-2026-05-22, external-dep-needed
  - **Approved**: 2026-05-22 operator directive ("Ok first of all yes approved, update tasks, vision, etc"). The strategic-decision gate is closed; the remaining block is external (OpenHands' Agent Canvas Initiative CLI ships June 1, 2026).
  - **Blocked**: needs-openhands-agent-canvas-cli-june-1-2026 (was: needs-operator-strategic-decision; now resolved).
  - **Milestone**: M2
  - **Competitive-goal**: closes the "no agent-tier benchmark advantage" gap. OpenHands publishes 65.8% SWE-bench Verified (Apr 2025); Minsky-via-Claude has no published score and is structurally unlikely to beat it (Claude Code's SWE-bench score is what Minsky inherits; OpenHands wraps the same LLM with a critic + best-of-N which Minsky's daemon shell doesn't do). Adding `openhands` as a backend lets the operator switch to OpenHands-via-Claude for tasks where the agent-tier delta matters, while keeping the daemon + TASKS.md + cross-repo fleet + constitution-as-CI on top. Net moat: 6/6 survive. See `competitors/openhands.md` § "Should we wrap OpenHands instead?" for the full analysis.
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/agent-config.ts` (add `openhands` to the agent matrix), `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/src/spawner.ts`, `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/src/index.ts`, `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/bin/minsky-openhands-spawn.py`, `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/README.md`, `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/package.json`, `novel/adapters/agent-runtime-openhands/tsconfig.json`, `AGENTS.md` § "Per-machine agent config — Agent support matrix" (add a 4th row for openhands), `~/.minsky/config.json` schema docs in `docs/configuration.md`, `bin/minsky` argv-builder for `openhands` (per-agent brief-delivery shape + `--model` flag passing), `test/integration/openhands-backend.test.ts` (new — integration test against a fixture task), `cloud-agent-config-audit-matrix` lint (already filed) to enforce the 4-agent contract.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-22 wrap-feasibility analysis (per rule #1 + operator directive 2026-05-22 "for every direct competitor you must deeply research should we replace part of minsky with that competitor's work") concluded: Shape A (agent-layer wrap as pluggable backend) is YES; Shape B (orchestrator-layer wrap via OpenHands Automations) is NO. Operator approved 2026-05-22. **The canonical Path C reshape plan lives at `docs/plans/2026-05-22-path-c-openhands-reshape.md`** — operator's day in the life, architectural before/after diagrams, config schema, what the daemon owns vs delegates, new failure modes + mitigations, 6-phase migration sequence, package-by-package fate mapping, lint-stack pruning framework. Read that doc before claiming this task; it's the contract for what this implementation produces. The implementation is straightforward (~1-2 weeks, mirrors the existing aider/devin/claude wiring), but the design depends on OpenHands' final June 1, 2026 CLI surface from the Agent Canvas Initiative (GitHub issue #14374). Unblock path post-approval: (a) wait for June 1 Dockerless CLI release, (b) audit the `openhands solve <task-brief>` interface for brief-delivery shape (stdin / `--prompt-file` / `--message-file`), (c) operator opens a tracked ticket so the PR can land per an internal review gate, (d) implement the integration per the 6-step sequence in the vision doc. Cross-references `monitor-openhands-agent-canvas-launch` (P2, already filed in PR #729) which tracks the June 1 launch + post-launch architecture audit.
  - **Hypothesis**: adding `openhands` as a pluggable backend gives Minsky operators a measurable agent-tier improvement (Claude-via-OpenHands SWE-bench score ≥10pp higher than Claude-via-bare-Minsky on the same task corpus) without regressing the orchestrator-tier moats. Falsifiable: if Claude-via-OpenHands does NOT beat Claude-via-bare-Minsky by ≥10pp, the agent-wrap rationale weakens.
  - **Success**: `~/.minsky/config.json` accepts `"cloud_agent": "openhands"`; integration test in `test/integration/openhands-backend.test.ts` exits 0 against a fixture task; the cloud-agent-config-audit-matrix lint expands to enforce the 4-agent contract; `bin/minsky` end-to-end test shows openhands spawning, running, and opening a PR on a sample host.
  - **Pivot**: if (a) OpenHands' Agent Canvas Initiative ships with a `solve <task-brief>` CLI shape that doesn't match Minsky's brief-delivery contract (stdin / `--prompt-file` / `--message-file`) and the adapter cost grows beyond 4 weeks, OR (b) the Claude-via-OpenHands SWE-bench delta over Claude-via-bare-Minsky measures <5pp at the end of a 2-week prototype — then revert to "openhands not a worthwhile backend" and document in `competitors/openhands.md` § "Should we wrap OpenHands instead?".
  - **Measurement**: `node novel/cross-repo-runner/test/cloud-agent-config-audit-matrix.test.mjs` reports a 4-row matrix (openhands present); `pnpm exec vitest run test/integration/openhands-backend.test.ts --reporter=basic` exits 0 on a fixture host; `node scripts/measure-claude-via-openhands-vs-bare.mjs --json | jq '.swe_bench_delta_pp >= 10'` returns true at end of 2-week prototype.
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent — OpenHands publishes 65.8% SWE-bench Verified, the right move is to inherit the agent capability, not build our own); operator directive 2026-05-22 ("for every direct competitor you must deeply research should we replace part of minsky with that competitor's work ... if yes, create a P0 human blocked task where you propose the change"); `competitors/openhands.md` § "Should we wrap OpenHands instead?" (the full strategic analysis); All-Hands AI, *SOTA on SWE-bench Verified with Inference-Time Scaling and Critic Model*, all-hands.dev/blog, 2025-04-15; OpenHands Agent Canvas Initiative, github.com/OpenHands/OpenHands#14374, 2026-05-11.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-22 wrap-feasibility analysis pass (PR #732); first application of the rule #1 wrap-feasibility discipline now encoded as Phase 7 in `.claude/skills/competitor-research/SKILL.md`.

- [ ] `agent-mediated-install` — any AI coding agent (Claude Code / Cursor / Windsurf / Devin / Codex / Ollama-via-aider) can install minsky for the operator's current folder in ≤60s with a single human prompt (telemetry consent), via a canonical `INSTALL.md` runbook colocated in the repo root
  - **ID**: agent-mediated-install
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Closing needs live 9-run real-agent matrix (claude/devin/cursor); deferred P2 + creds absent
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, install, dx, agent-ux, telemetry, operator-directive, observed-2026-05-20
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 — "user is working in claude/devin/windsurf/ollama/cursor, asks their agent to install minsky and get it running for current folder. Agent should find minsky repo, read its instructions, quickly do that, asking questions only where absolutely necessary, including agreement to submit anonymized runtime logs. Save answers + submit them to minsky's DB of which projects agreed and at what time. Then run minsky or tell user installation is complete. This installation path should be preferred and recommended above other info." Existing `minsky-init-one-command-bootstrap` (P0 — npx/curl) and `minsky-npx-install-and-run` (P1 — one shell line) remain alternative paths for users without an agent handy; this task makes the agent-mediated path the *canonical* one.
  - **Hypothesis**: most new minsky operators are already inside an AI coding agent when they hear about minsky. Shipping an agent-readable `INSTALL.md` (LLM-targeted prose with explicit prerequisites, shell commands, consent prompt, rollback) plus a `minsky consent` subcommand that records the operator's telemetry decision locally AND submits to a minsky-owned consent ledger collapses install from 10+ min (read README, choose path, debug Node version, register host) to ≤60s (paste one prompt into the agent, answer one yes/no consent question). Measured by p95 time-from-prompt-to-first-iteration AND prompts-asked-per-install across 3 agent providers.
  - **Success**: An agent (claude-code, devin, cursor) reading INSTALL.md on a fresh repo completes install + first iteration in ≤90s with exactly 1 human prompt (the telemetry consent), measured across 3 providers and 3 fresh repos each (9 runs). Success = all 9 runs hit threshold AND consent record exists in `~/.minsky/telemetry-consent.json` with valid `{consent, timestamp, host_path_hash, agent}` fields AND (when telemetry server endpoint exists) is mirrored to the consent ledger. Failure modes that count against success: any run requiring >1 human prompt, any run >90s, any run leaving the system broken (consent file partial-written, daemon not started, PATH not updated).
  - **Pivot**: if 2+ of {claude-code, devin, cursor} require >2 human prompts or >120s p95 across 3 runs each, abandon the agent-mediated path as the *canonical* install (keep INSTALL.md as a reference document) and ship `npx minsky` (P1 `minsky-npx-install-and-run`) as the recommended one-line install instead.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs --providers=claude-code,devin,cursor --runs-per-provider=3 --threshold-seconds=90 --threshold-prompts=1` — script exits 0 only if all 9 runs hit threshold, emits per-run JSON with timing + prompt counts.
  - **Anchor**: Nottingham, Mark. *Well-Known Uniform Resource Identifiers (URIs)* (RFC 8615), IETF, May 2019 — colocated machine-readable metadata at a stable conventional path is the canonical pattern for agent-discoverable instructions. Composes with rule #16 (default by default — the agent-mediated path is the default install) and `docs/PRACTICES.md` (this task ships an applied practice = "agent-readable install instruction at a conventional path").
  - **Details**: Vertical slice in 3 sub-deliverables. (1) **`INSTALL.md` (repo root)** — ships as a stub in this PR; closes this task when it covers: prerequisites verification (node ≥22, pnpm ≥9, git ≥2.40, exact commands), clone + install steps with exact `<minsky-repo>` canonical path, host registration via `~/.minsky/config.json`, telemetry consent prompt (verbatim wording), daemon start, confirm-to-human checklist, failure-mode escape hatches, explicit out-of-scope list (no task picking, no remote pushes). (2) **`minsky consent` subcommand** — new `bin/minsky` case + `novel/tick-loop/src/cli-consent.ts`. Reads `--yes` or `--no`, writes atomic JSON to `~/.minsky/telemetry-consent.json` (tmp + rename), POSTs to `MINSKY_TELEMETRY_ENDPOINT` when configured (local-first; server submission best-effort, never blocks). Tests cover first-write, idempotent re-write, atomic-on-crash, server-unavailable, endpoint-unset. (3) **`scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs`** — measurement harness; spawns each agent provider against a fresh tmp-repo with INSTALL.md, records timings + prompt counts, emits JSON. Required by the Measurement field; fixture-tested against mock agent CLIs.
  - **Files**: INSTALL.md (new — partial in this PR, finished by this task), bin/minsky (new `consent` subcommand), novel/tick-loop/src/cli-consent.ts (new) + sibling test, scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs (new) + sibling test, README.md (Getting started reorg landed in this PR; this task closes the loop by making INSTALL.md actually deliver), vision.md (add a Pattern-index row mapping INSTALL.md to RFC 8615).
  - **Touches**: INSTALL.md, bin/minsky, novel/tick-loop/src/cli-consent.ts, scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs, README.md, vision.md
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `node scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs --providers=claude-code,devin,cursor --runs-per-provider=3 --threshold-seconds=90 --threshold-prompts=1` exits 0. (2) `cat ~/.minsky/telemetry-consent.json` after install shows valid record with all 4 fields. (3) An operator who reads ONLY the README (not this task body) can copy the agent-mediated prompt and it works first-try without further reading. (4) `minsky consent --no` correctly records dissent without breaking the install. (5) When `MINSKY_TELEMETRY_ENDPOINT` is set, a POST appears in the server's access log with the consent payload (consent / timestamp / host_path_hash / agent only — no PII).
  - **Risk**: medium. (a) Privacy: telemetry endpoint accepts only the documented fields. Mitigation: SHA-256-hash host_path with a per-machine salt before submitting; only the hash + a machine-id-derived hash go to the server, never the raw path. (b) Agent diversity: claude-code / devin / cursor have different transcript conventions — the measurement harness needs per-provider prompt-count parsers. Mitigation: each provider gets a fixture-tested parser module. (c) Adoption: if the path is too magical, control-loving operators may bounce — keep manual fallback prominent in README's "Manual install" section.
  - **Note**: Server-submission half of sub-deliverable (2) is blocked on a hosting decision for the consent endpoint — file `minsky-telemetry-consent-server-hosting` as a P1 sub-task. Local-only consent recording is enough to unblock this task's M1 milestone. **Progress 2026-05-23**: slice (1) shipped via PR #745 (`INSTALL.md` at repo root); slice (2) shipped via PR #747 (`minsky consent --yes/--no` CLI + 10 integration tests); slice (3) mock-mode shipped via PR #748 (`scripts/measure-agent-install.mjs` + 14 tests + wired into `pre-pr-lint --stage=full`). Remaining work to fully close this P0: live-mode for real-agent invocation (P2 follow-up `measure-agent-install-live-mode`) + at least one passing 9-run snapshot in `.minsky/measurements/`. The mock-mode CI gate is now load-bearing; the live-mode gap is the credibility-against-competitors gap.

- [ ] `fake-data-and-deprecation-marker-discipline` — every stub / mock / hardcoded-placeholder in `novel/*` source code carries a canonical `// FAKE:` marker (reason + linked task id + date) at the point of definition; every `@deprecated` JSDoc export carries the parallel `// DEPRECATED:` marker (replacement + removal milestone + linked task id); a CI linter rejects unmarked stubs in `novel/*/src/`; `docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md` is the central registry, drift between markers and registry is a CI failure. Prevents agents (or humans) from accidentally building on top of unfinished mocks
  - **ID**: fake-data-and-deprecation-marker-discipline
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, rule-18, discipline, anti-stub, deprecation, operator-directive, observed-2026-05-20, blocked-2026-05-23
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator-decision — task spec claims this discipline will become `rule #18` of the constitution, but rule #18 in `vision.md:211` is already taken by "Merge means MERGE — no close-with-preservation shortcuts" (iron, no exemption — landed pre-2026-05-23). Cannot ship this task's `scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs` because the rule-number collision would silently shadow either the merge-discipline lint or the fake-data lint depending on which loads first. Operator must decide: (A) renumber THIS task's rule to #19 (and rename all referenced files / lint scripts / fixtures from `rule-18-*` to `rule-19-*`), (B) renumber the existing "Merge means MERGE" rule to a different number (high disruption — that rule is cited by `pr-merge-no-shortcuts` skill, several PRs, and is currently iron-bar-graded), or (C) abandon the rule-number framing for this discipline and use a non-numbered name like `check-fake-marker.mjs`. Block lifts when operator picks A / B / C.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 — "in minsky all fake data and all deprecations should be always explicitly marked, so that we don't rely on temporary mock of unfinished task by mistake. Be realistic about it too." The "realistic" part is iron: the linter catches OBVIOUS stub patterns (literal returns, suspicious config constants, `@deprecated` JSDoc); it does NOT claim to catch LLM-hallucinated code that looks real but isn't. Failure-mode #9 in user-story 011 documents this limitation explicitly. The marker discipline is mechanical for the easy cases; the hard cases (semantic-fakes) still require code review.
  - **Hypothesis**: at the point of definition, every stub in `novel/*/src/` carries a one-line marker with three required fields (reason + backticked task id + date). A heuristic CI linter (`scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs`) detects the obvious stub patterns and rejects PRs that introduce them without the marker. Test code is exempt by path (`*.test.ts`, `*.fixture.ts`, `test/fixtures/`, `**/__tests__/`). The `docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md` central index is co-maintained: every marker in code has a row, every row has a marker. Drift between the two is a CI failure. Measured by `fake_data_registry_size` trending DOWN over 4 weeks post-backfill (the registry is a punch list that gets shorter, not a permanent feature).
  - **Success**: (1) Linter ships at `scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs` with sibling tests covering all 10 failure modes in user-story 011's chaos table. (2) Initial backfill sweep marks every existing stub in `novel/*/src/` (count TBD — early estimate 8-15 entries based on a manual scan); the backfill is its own task (`fake-data-initial-backfill-sweep` P1, filed by this task). (3) `docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md` has the corresponding rows. (4) Linter is wired into `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` at `--stage=full`. (5) The grep-based marker-presence check (cheap pass) runs at `--stage=fast`. (6) After 8 weeks, `fake_data_registry_size` declines for ≥4 consecutive weeks. (7) The user-story 011 integration test passes against the shipped linter.
  - **Pivot**: if the heuristic linter has a false-positive rate >20% during backfill (operator has to add `// not-fake:` opt-out on more than 1-in-5 detections), the heuristic is too aggressive — narrow the detection rules: drop the "suspicious config constants" branch (often false-positive on legitimate enums / status codes), keep only the literal-return-with-no-I/O detection and the `@deprecated` JSDoc check. If THAT still has >10% false positive, abandon the linter and ship only the marker convention + registry discipline (operator-enforced via PR review, not CI). Threshold: count opt-out markers added during the first 4 weeks; if `opt-out_count / detection_count` exceeds 20%, narrow scope.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs --strict 2>&1 | tee /tmp/rule-18.log; grep -c "^### " docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md; grep -rcE "// (FAKE|DEPRECATED):" novel/ bin/ | awk -F: '{s+=$2}END{print s}'` — the first command exits 0 only when there's no drift; the second + third must match (registry size = marker count). Wired as one assertion in `scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs --measure`.
  - **Anchor**: Hunt & Thomas, *The Pragmatic Programmer* (Addison-Wesley 1999), Ch. 8 — "no broken windows": every unmarked stub is a broken window. Composed with rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — every rule is a CI lint, not a hope) and Beck *Extreme Programming Explained* 1999 Ch. 17 (visible debt is debt that gets paid; the registry is the debt list).
  - **Details**: Vertical slice in 4 sub-deliverables. (1) **vision.md rule #18 + AGENTS.md update** — add the new rule + marker convention spec to the constitution. Agents read AGENTS.md on startup; the marker discipline becomes part of their default behaviour. (2) **`scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs` + sibling test** — heuristic linter with `--fixture` / `--registry` / `--strict` flags; AST walk via `@typescript-eslint/parser` (or simpler regex pass on `.ts` source if AST is overkill for the heuristics); detects literal-return functions, `@deprecated` JSDoc tags, suspicious config constants. (3) **`docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md`** — the central index. Format mirrors `DEPRECATED.md`: one H3 per entry with file path, marker text quoted, task id linked, date added. (4) **Backfill** — file `fake-data-initial-backfill-sweep` (P1) that runs the linter in warn-mode for one week, captures all current offenders, lands canonical markers + registry rows for them, then flips the linter to fail-mode in a follow-up commit.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-rule-18-explicit-fake-marker.mjs` (new) + paired test, `docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md` (new), `vision.md` (add rule #18 section), `AGENTS.md` (add marker convention to the agent-readable rules), `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (wire the new check into `fast` + `full` stages), `user-stories/011-fake-data-marked-explicitly.test.ts` (the integration test from the story; ships with `describe.skipIf` until the linter lands), `test/fixtures/fake-data/{good-stub,bad-stub,false-positive,bad-deprecation,good-deprecation,drift-marker-only,drift-registry-only}/` (new fixtures).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/`, `docs/`, `vision.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `user-stories/`, `test/fixtures/`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` passes on `origin/main` after the backfill sweep lands. (2) `pnpm vitest run user-stories/011-fake-data-marked-explicitly.test.ts` exits 0 with all 10 failure-mode fixtures passing. (3) `docs/FAKE-DATA-REGISTRY.md` has ≥1 entry (the initial backfill must find at least one existing stub to be credible — the manual scan estimate is 8-15). (4) `vision.md` § "Pattern conformance index" has a row for the linter. (5) A test PR that intentionally adds an unmarked stub fails the lint; adding the canonical marker + registry row makes it pass.
  - **Risk**: medium-high. (a) **False-positive rate during backfill**: the heuristic is approximate; legitimate constants (`HTTP_OK = 200`, enum values, immutable defaults) will trip it. Mitigation: the `// not-fake: <reason>` opt-out + the pivot threshold (>20% opt-out rate triggers narrowing). (b) **Backfill volume**: the initial sweep may find significantly more than the estimated 8-15 stubs (could be 30+). Mitigation: backfill is its own task; budget two days for it; landing canonical markers is mechanical once the convention is documented. (c) **Drift over time**: stubs that get replaced via PR can leave orphan registry rows. Mitigation: the bidirectional drift check (rows-without-markers fails the lint just like markers-without-rows). (d) **Agent behaviour gap**: agents not in this codebase's AGENTS.md context may not know about the marker convention and write unmarked stubs. Mitigation: the linter catches them at PR time; the rejection message includes the canonical marker example so the agent can self-correct.
  - **Note**: composes with rule #10 (deterministic enforcement), rule #11 (no flaky load-bearing metric — `fake_data_registry_size` is deliberately simple), rule #17 (proactive healing — the linter IS the heal). The user-story 011 is the spec; this task is the implementation. Files `fake-data-initial-backfill-sweep` (P1) as a sub-task.

- [ ] `minsky-human-comm-via-file` — minsky has no first-class human↔agent communication channel; operator wants the simplest possible mechanism: a plain file where agents write questions and humans write answers, with file-change watching on both sides
  - **ID**: minsky-human-comm-via-file
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, ux, dx, human-loop, operator-directive, rule-1, observed-2026-05-20, decomposed-2026-05-23
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Decomposition 2026-05-23**: parent broken into 4 ship-independent vertical slices. Parent stays open until all 4 ship + an operator-side live verification passes.
    - ✅ Sub-task 1 `human-loop-qa-log-format` shipped 2026-05-23 PR #755 (`novel/human-loop/package.json` + `novel/human-loop/tsconfig.json` + `novel/human-loop/README.md` + pure parser/serializer at `novel/human-loop/src/qa-log-format.ts` + 12 sibling tests at `novel/human-loop/src/qa-log-format.test.ts` covering all 8 documented cases + 4 bonus edge cases).
    - ✅ Sub-task 2 `human-loop-ask-human-and-watcher` shipped 2026-05-23 PR #756 (`novel/human-loop/src/ask-human.ts` async API + `fs.watch` 100ms-debounce + atomic `fs.appendFile` for multi-agent safety + `TimeoutError` class + 8 sibling tests at `novel/human-loop/src/ask-human.test.ts` covering happy path, timeout, taskId-isolation, stale-answer-ignored, race-condition, and debounce). Pivoted from `proper-lockfile` per parent's Success criterion #5 "or equivalent" clause — `fs.appendFile` is atomic for payloads under PIPE_BUF (4KB Linux, 512B POSIX) which a Q block fits well within. If multi-agent contention becomes an issue under live load, file `human-loop-proper-lockfile-upgrade` as P1.
    - ✅ Sub-task 3 `human-loop-minsky-qa-subcommand` shipped 2026-05-23 (`bin/minsky qa` subcommand — `--print-path`, `--init-only`, `--help` flags + bare-`qa` opens $EDITOR + tail -F; honors `MINSKY_QA_LOG_PATH` env override). 10 sibling integration tests at `test/integration/qa.test.ts` covering print-path, init-only-create, init-only-preserve, parent-dir-creation, unknown-flag-exit-2, help, env-override, format-conformance, combined-flags, no-editor-side-effect. The `minsky watch` pending-Q count integration is split out as sub-task 3.5 `human-loop-watch-pending-q-count` (P1 follow-up, filed) so this slice ships clean without touching the dashboard.
    - ✅ Sub-task 4 `human-loop-brief-template-and-docs` shipped 2026-05-23 (3 surfaces): (a) `buildDaemonBrief` in `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` gains a new "Asking the operator a question" section between the iteration directive and the pre-PR lint-stack gate — agents reading the brief now learn to prefer the QA channel over filing `Blocked: needs-user-approval` when the operator is reachable; (b) README.md "Why Minsky" list gains a 4th bullet pointing operators at `novel/human-loop/README.md`; (c) `vision.md` Pattern conformance index gains row 105 for `novel/human-loop/` citing Cockburn 2001 (ask-wait-branch) + Helland 2007 (event log) + Gamma 1994 (Observer). Tests for the new brief section deferred to follow-up `daemon-test-biome-useawait-cleanup` (P3, filed in same commit) — 17 pre-existing biome `useAwait` warnings in `daemon.test.ts` block any new test addition to that file under the `--error-on-warnings` pre-commit gate; ship the cleanup as its own scope-disciplined PR. Parent P0 stays open pending operator-side live verification — the implicit acceptance criterion is one full Q→A round-trip via `minsky qa` that an agent picks up and resumes from.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 reviewing README — "where does it mention how minsky communicates with humans? I need it to be as simple as creating a log or xml or whatever file where you leave questions and I leave answers and you read them on file change". Today minsky communicates with humans through three weak channels: (a) `**Blocked**: needs-user-approval` / `needs-human-action` markers in TASKS.md task bodies (humans have to grep for them); (b) draft PRs that the human reviews; (c) `daemon.log` warnings. None of these support fast, back-and-forth Q&A — they're all "agent files and waits up to N hours for the next human pass". The operator wants a low-latency file the agent can write a question to and watch for the human's answer, like a chat transcript on disk.
  - **Hypothesis**: a single append-only Markdown file at `.minsky/qa-log.md` in the host repo (with sibling `.minsky/qa-log.json` for structured agent reads) acts as the channel. Agent writes `## Q: <iso-ts>\n<question>\n` AND waits up to N minutes for the human to append `## A: <iso-ts>\n<answer>\n` to the same file. Both sides watch via `fs.watch` (Node) and `chokidar` is unnecessary — `fs.watch` covers the macOS + Linux case; pivot to chokidar if `fs.watch` produces spurious events. Default timeout: 4 hours (the operator's usual working day). On timeout, the agent files a `**Blocked**: waiting-for-qa-answer-<timestamp>` entry in TASKS.md and moves on. Post-fix, operators report a "minsky asked me X and I answered, then it kept going" experience in ≥80% of human-blocked questions, vs the current 0% (every blocked task today requires the human to re-engage on the next daily/weekly pass).
  - **Success**: (1) Agent-side: `await askHuman(question, { timeoutMs: 4 * 3600_000 })` appends to `.minsky/qa-log.md` and returns the human's answer string when the file changes with a matching `## A:` block. (2) Human-side: editing `.minsky/qa-log.md` in any editor, saving, triggers the agent's `fs.watch` listener within ≤500 ms. (3) Round-trip latency: ≤2 minutes from human typing the answer to the agent receiving it (90th percentile). (4) Visible signal in `minsky watch` dashboard: pending Q count. (5) Multi-agent safety: when 2 agents ask questions concurrently, both Q blocks are appended cleanly (no interleaving) via file-locking (`proper-lockfile` or equivalent).
  - **Pivot**: if `fs.watch` produces too many spurious events on the operator's macOS box (>10/hour), switch to polling-with-100ms-interval (`fs.statSync(file).mtimeMs` change detection — battery-friendly enough for an interactive surface). If the Markdown format is too brittle for the agent's parsing (e.g., humans answer in the middle of a Q block by accident), add a structured `.minsky/qa-log.jsonl` sidecar AND parse the JSON for the answer routing; keep the Markdown for human-friendly rendering. If the channel is unused (<5 Q events/week after rollout), retire it — operators have shown they prefer TASKS.md `Blocked` markers.
  - **Measurement**: `wc -l .minsky/qa-log.md` rises after every agent ask (each Q adds ≥2 lines); `grep -c "^## Q:" .minsky/qa-log.md` and `grep -c "^## A:" .minsky/qa-log.md` should be within ±1 of each other (in flight: Q-only briefly); round-trip latency observable in `.minsky/qa-events.jsonl` (one event per Q-asked / A-received) — p90 ≤120s.
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent — Markdown + `fs.watch` are the simplest possible primitives; chat protocols, websocket subprotocols, MCP-prompt resources all over-engineer the operator's "just leave answers in a file" request); rule #16 (default by default — the channel is on by default; the agent uses it whenever a question would otherwise block); rule #6 (let-it-crash — if the file is corrupt or unwritable, the agent falls back to the existing `Blocked: needs-user-approval` TASKS.md path); Cockburn 2001 *Writing Effective Use Cases* (the "ask, wait, branch on answer" pattern is a use-case extension — model it as such).
  - **Details**: (a) New module `novel/human-loop/` package (workspace member). Exports `askHuman(question: string, opts: AskOpts): Promise<string>`. Pure orchestrator + injected `FileSystem` seam for tests. (b) File format — Markdown with stable section headers + a JSONL sidecar for machine reads. Q section: `## Q: <task-id> · <iso-ts>\n**from**: <agent>\n**asks**: <multiline question text>\n`. A section: `## A: <task-id> · <iso-ts>\n<multiline answer text>\n`. (c) Watch mechanism: `fs.watch(qaLogPath, { persistent: true })` + debounce 100 ms. (d) Concurrency: `proper-lockfile` (third-party dep, rule #2 row required) wraps the append. (e) Wire into `bin/minsky watch` to show pending Q count + colour-tint the dashboard when ≥1 Q is unanswered. (f) Agent surface — `novel/cross-repo-runner` brief template gains a "If you need to ask the operator a question, write it to `.minsky/qa-log.md` via the `ask-human` tool" instruction; the tool is the `askHuman` function above. (g) Operator surface — `minsky qa` subcommand opens `.minsky/qa-log.md` in `$EDITOR` and `tail -F`'s it after exit. (h) Bookkeeping: every Q/A pair appended to `.minsky/qa-events.jsonl` with `{ ts, taskId, q, a, latencyMs }` for the dashboard's pending-Q count and the success-measurement p90.
  - **Files**: `novel/human-loop/package.json` (new workspace package), `novel/human-loop/src/ask-human.ts` + `.test.ts`, `novel/human-loop/src/qa-log-format.ts` + `.test.ts`, `novel/human-loop/src/file-watcher.ts` + `.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (brief template addition), `bin/minsky` (`qa` subcommand), `bin/minsky` (`watch` adds pending-Q count), `README.md` (new "How minsky communicates with humans" section), `vision.md` (new row in Pattern conformance index for `novel/human-loop`).
  - **Touches**: `novel/human-loop/**`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs`, `bin/minsky`, `README.md`, `vision.md`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) Integration test: agent calls `askHuman("Should I proceed?")` in a fixture, separate test process appends a `## A: ...` block to the qa-log; assert the agent's promise resolves with the answer text within 500 ms. (2) Live verification: type `minsky qa` in iTerm, see the Markdown file open in `$EDITOR`, type an answer, save, observe the daemon log `qa-log: answer received for task <id>`. (3) Multi-agent: spawn 2 fixture agents concurrently asking different questions; both Q blocks land cleanly with no interleaving (lockfile contract).
  - **Risk**: medium. `fs.watch` semantics differ subtly on macOS (FSEvents) vs Linux (inotify). Macos can fire 2 events per save (atomic write via temp+rename); Linux fires 1. Mitigation: dedupe events within 100 ms by content hash. Also: humans may edit the file in non-blessed ways (insert text, edit a previous Q) — the parser must be resilient to that, OR the format must be tolerant. Lean on append-only convention (humans only append to the bottom).
  - **Note**: composes with TASKS.md's existing `Blocked: needs-user-approval` markers — the QA channel is the fast path; TASKS.md is the durable fallback for long-running waits. Operators who don't watch the QA file get the same Blocked task notification as today.
