- [ ] `minsky-uninstall-clean-removal` — `minsky uninstall` removes everything minsky added to a repo and machine with zero residue
  - **ID**: minsky-uninstall-clean-removal
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, ux, install, trust, blocked-2026-05-23
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator-decision — 3 spec criteria conflict with PR #743's deliberate design choices. (1) Criterion (b) "remove `.minsky/` sidecar from current repo" CONFLICTS with PR #743's explicit preservation of per-repo `.minsky/` as operator data (the one-command-uninstall flow says "host repo data (.minsky/ inside your repos) is untouched"). (2) Criterion (d) "remove `~/.minsky/` (with `--global` flag, not by default)" CONFLICTS with PR #743's behavior which removes `~/.minsky/` BY DEFAULT (no --global flag). (3) Criterion (e) "remove PATH shim" is not implemented — PR #743 leaves the PATH shim (added by `minsky init` to `~/.zshrc` etc.) in place. Operator must decide which spec wins: (A) update this task's spec to match shipped behavior (preserve per-repo data, default-purge global, leave PATH shim), or (B) extend PR #743 with a `--with-host-data` flag for criterion (b), revert criterion (d) to require `--global`, and add PATH-shim removal. Block lifts when the operator picks A or B.
  - **Competitive-goal**: clean uninstall builds trust — a developer who can't easily remove a tool won't install it; no competitor (Devin/OpenHands/SWE-agent) offers a clean uninstall path either, so this is a differentiator.
  - **Details**: `minsky uninstall` should: (a) stop any running daemon (`minsky stop`); (b) remove `.minsky/` sidecar from the current repo; (c) remove launchd/systemd units; (d) remove `~/.minsky/` global config (with `--global` flag, not by default); (e) remove PATH shim; (f) print what was removed and confirm `git status` is clean. Never remove tracked files or user code.
  - **Files**: `bin/minsky-uninstall` (new), paired tests verifying complete cleanup
  - **Touches**: bin/minsky-uninstall, test/**/*uninstall*
  - **Hypothesis**: today there is no uninstall path; users must manually find and remove files. After this, `minsky uninstall` leaves zero residue.
  - **Success**: after `minsky uninstall`, `find . -name '.minsky' -o -name 'minsky' | grep -v node_modules | grep -v .git` returns nothing; `git status --porcelain` is empty; no launchd/systemd units remain.
  - **Pivot**: if full cleanup is complex (e.g., shared node_modules), implement `minsky uninstall --list` that shows what would be removed and lets the user confirm.
  - **Measurement**: after uninstall, a `minsky doctor` or `which minsky` returns not-found; `git status` clean.
  - **Anchor**: npm `npm uninstall` convention; Homebrew `brew uninstall --zap` (complete removal pattern).

- [ ] `minsky-default-8h-repo-transformation` — `minsky` with no flags runs an 8h session that converts any repo toward minsky standards: creates tasks, does deep research, adds metrics baseline, updates docs, marks unsafe operations as human-blocked
  - **ID**: minsky-default-8h-repo-transformation
  - **Tags**: p0, milestone-m1, core-workflow, cross-repo, ux
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: no competitor offers a "point at any repo and improve it for 8 hours" mode — Devin does single tasks, OpenHands does single tasks, Aider is interactive. This is minsky's unique value proposition.
  - **Details**: the default `minsky` run (no flags) should: (a) bootstrap the repo if not already done; (b) establish a metrics baseline (test count, coverage, lint health, build status, dependency age, doc coverage) and write it to `.minsky/baseline.json`; (c) do deep research on the repo (read README, understand structure, identify patterns); (d) create tasks in TASKS.md based on findings (missing tests, stale docs, security issues, dependency updates, code smells); (e) work through the task queue for up to 8h; (f) never execute dangerous operations (force push, delete branches, modify secrets, rm -rf) — instead mark them as `**Blocked**: needs-human-action — <reason>`; (g) at the end, produce a `minsky report` showing before/after delta on all baseline metrics. The 8h limit is the default; overridable with `--max-hours=N`.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/default-session.ts` (new — the 8h session orchestrator), `scripts/baseline-metrics.mjs` (new — metrics snapshot), `scripts/minsky-report.mjs` (new — before/after delta), paired tests
  - **Touches**: novel/tick-loop/src/default-session.ts, scripts/baseline-metrics.mjs, scripts/minsky-report.mjs, test/**/*default-session*
  - **Hypothesis**: a fixture repo with no TASKS.md and basic issues (missing tests, stale docs) gains ≥10 filed tasks and ≥3 merged improvements after one 8h default session.
  - **Success**: on a fixture repo: baseline captured, ≥10 tasks filed, ≥3 PRs merged, 0 dangerous operations executed, report shows measurable improvement on ≥2 metrics.
  - **Pivot**: if 8h is too ambitious for M1, reduce to a 2h "quick assessment" mode that only does (a)-(d) + report, deferring (e) to explicit `minsky run`.
  - **Measurement**: `minsky report --json` on the fixture repo before/after; task count, PR count, metric deltas.
  - **Anchor**: Ries 2011 *Lean Startup* (build-measure-learn — the baseline + delta IS the learn loop); Forsgren/Humble/Kim 2018 (DORA — the metrics ARE the DORA four keys applied to the repo).

  - **Pivot**: if users reject the submission flow, make it fully opt-in with a config flag and focus on local-only findings in TASKS.md.
  - **Measurement**: count of externally-submitted findings per week after launch.
  - **Anchor**: Mozilla Crash Reporter (opt-in telemetry pattern); VSCode telemetry (transparent + anonymized).

- [ ] `minsky-on-minsky-as-regular-host` — minsky's own repo is a regular host destination (not special-cased), including remote task submission from other machines; full dogfood parity
  - **ID**: minsky-on-minsky-as-regular-host
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Premise false: novel/tick-loop/ package and minsky.mjs edit target do not exist in repo

  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: "we use our own product, on itself, the same way you would use it on your repo" is the strongest possible credibility signal. No competitor does this (Devin doesn't run Devin on Devin's codebase as a regular host).
  - **Details**: today minsky-on-itself is special: `pnpm minsky:setup` runs a custom supervisor path that differs from `minsky --host <minsky-repo>`. This task makes the minsky repo a regular host: (a) `minsky bootstrap <minsky-repo>` creates the standard `.minsky/` sidecar (already exists but with custom config); (b) `minsky --host <minsky-repo>` runs the standard cross-repo-runner, not a special minsky:setup path; (c) `minsky submit-finding --to <minsky-repo>` works from any other machine, adding tasks to minsky's own TASKS.md via the standard remote submission flow (compose `minsky-remote-task-submission`); (d) the weekly benchmark (`weekly-lmarena-style-benchmark`) runs against the minsky repo as one of its benchmark hosts; (e) `pnpm minsky:setup` becomes an alias for `minsky --host . --daemon` (backward compat, not a separate codepath). This is an experiment: if running minsky-on-minsky via the standard path produces worse results than the custom minsky:setup path, the experiment fails and we keep the custom path (document why).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (remove dogfood special-casing), `package.json` (dogfood script becomes alias), `setup.sh` (simplify — delegate to `minsky init`), paired tests verifying the standard host path works on the minsky repo
  - **Touches**: novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs, package.json, setup.sh, novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.test.ts
  - **Hypothesis**: today the minsky:setup path is special-cased (~50 lines of dogfood-only logic in setup.sh + package.json). After this, `minsky --host .` on the minsky repo produces identical behavior to `pnpm minsky:setup`, and remote task submission works from other machines.
  - **Success**: `minsky --host <minsky-repo> --once --dry-run` picks a task from minsky's TASKS.md and produces a RunnerPlan; `minsky submit-finding --to <minsky-repo> --preview` from a second machine shows the submission preview; `pnpm minsky:setup` is a one-line alias that calls `minsky --host . --daemon`.
  - **Pivot**: if the standard host path can't handle minsky's complex monorepo (pnpm workspaces, 180 test files, 26 lint scripts), keep a thin `minsky.config.yaml` at repo root that configures the host-specific behavior — but it must be the same config format any other host would use, not a private API.
  - **Measurement**: `diff <(minsky --host . --once --dry-run 2>&1) <(pnpm minsky:setup --once --dry-run 2>&1)` produces no functional differences (output format may differ, but task picked + plan shape must match).
  - **Anchor**: Kernighan & Pike *The Practice of Programming* 1999 ("use your own software"); Raymond *The Cathedral and the Bazaar* 1999 ("eating your own dog food"); rule #1 (don't maintain two paths when one will do — the minsky:setup path IS the standard path, or it exposes a gap in the standard path).

- [ ] `runany-zero-arg-entrypoint` — `minsky` with NO args, run in any folder, starts the orchestrator scoped to that folder + all subfolders (no params ever required)
  - **ID**: runany-zero-arg-entrypoint

Builds on `minsky-cli-context-aware-ux`.

- [ ] `minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap` — `git clone && pnpm install && minsky daemon doctor` works on a fresh checkout with no manual `pnpm build` step
  - **ID**: minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED; block retained — test files freeform-cite this id; remove citation then block.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, bootstrap, fresh-clone, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: protects `bootstrap-success-rate` (fraction of fresh clones that reach a runnable `minsky` without operator intervention) — a broken first run on a no-credits machine means the operator abandons that machine entirely.
  - **Hypothesis**: On a fresh clone the bash shim `bin/minsky` delegates to `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run` / `bin/minsky-run.sh`, which needs the TS workspaces built. Root `package.json` already runs `prepare: tsc -b --force` on install, but there is no regression pinning it, and a missing build (interrupted install, partial tree) still surfaces as a raw node `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND` instead of an actionable hint. Pre-registration: post-fix, on a fresh clone, `pnpm install` ALONE leaves `pnpm minsky daemon doctor` exiting 0; if a built dist is missing, `bin/minsky` emits a one-line `minsky: run \`pnpm install\` from the repo root` hint instead of a node stack trace; a bats test pins both branches.
  - **Success**: a new `tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats` asserts (a) root `package.json` carries a `prepare` script that runs `tsc -b`, and (b) `bin/minsky` prints an actionable hint (not a raw node module-resolution error) when an expected built entrypoint is absent; the bats suite exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the `prepare`/`tsc -b` build proves too brittle on a partial dependency tree (noisy logs, CI semantics), demote to a `setup.sh` step (`pnpm install && pnpm -r build`) the operator runs once after clone; keep the bin/minsky actionable-hint backstop either way.
  - **Measurement**: `bats tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats 2>&1 | grep -qE '0 failures' && grep -qE '\"prepare\".*tsc -b' package.json`
  - **Anchor**: pnpm docs — the `prepare` lifecycle hook is the canonical build-on-install mechanism; Armstrong, *Making Reliable Distributed Systems in the Presence of Software Errors*, 2003 — loud-fail at the actionable boundary (a clear hint) over a silent ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND.
  - **Details**: (a) Verify/keep the root `package.json` `prepare: tsc -b --force` build-on-install. (b) Add a dist/entrypoint-existence guard near the top of `bin/minsky`: if the resolved run target (`novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run` or `bin/minsky-run.sh`) is missing or unbuilt, write a one-line actionable hint to stderr and exit 1 instead of letting node emit a module-resolution stack trace. (c) New `tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats` pinning the `prepare` script presence and the actionable-hint branch (use a temp HOME/repo copy or a missing-target stub — do NOT `rm -rf` a shared dist, to avoid racing concurrent test runs). (d) Update `README.md` Installation + `AGENTS.md` Repository setup with the `git clone && pnpm install && minsky` flow (no separate build step).
  - **Files**: `tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats` (new), `bin/minsky` (entrypoint-existence guard + actionable hint), `package.json` (confirm/keep `prepare`), `README.md` (Installation), `AGENTS.md` (Repository setup).
  - **Touches**: tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats, bin/minsky, package.json, README.md, AGENTS.md
  - **Acceptance**: (a) `bats tests/fresh-clone-bootstrap.bats` exits 0; (b) `bin/minsky` prints an actionable hint (not a node stack trace) when the run target is missing; (c) `package.json` keeps a `prepare` script running `tsc -b`; (d) docs show the no-build-step flow; (e) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.
  - **Composes-with**: `minsky-runtime-resilience` (sibling self-healing slice — same loud-fail-at-the-right-boundary discipline in the bash CLI).
- [ ] `minsky-runtime-resilience` — graceful-degrade on unwritable state dirs / log paths / missing run-script so `bin/minsky-run.sh` fails at the operator-actionable boundary, never with a raw shell error
  - **ID**: minsky-runtime-resilience
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED; block retained — test files freeform-cite this id; remove citation then block.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, runtime, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: protects `daemon-uptime` on multi-machine syncs — a runtime I/O failure (wrong-owner MINSKY_HOME, read-only mount) currently aborts an iteration with a bare shell errno instead of a recovery hint, costing operator debugging time on the very machines minsky is meant to keep alive.
  - **Hypothesis**: Live runtime failure modes still abort `bin/minsky-run.sh` with a raw shell/errno instead of operator-actionable output: (i) the experiment-store `mkdir -p` (the `INVARIANT FAIL: cannot create $dir` path) gives no recovery command; (ii) a brief/log file write under an unwritable dir aborts the iteration instead of falling back to `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}`; (iii) a missing/non-executable run target (`bin/minsky-run.sh` itself, or the openhands spawn shim) surfaces as `command not found` / `ENOENT` with no pointer at the fix. Pre-registration: post-fix, when the experiment-store dir is unwritable, the runner emits a one-line stderr line naming the path + a recovery hint (`chmod u+w <path>` or set `MINSKY_HOME=<writable>`) and exits non-zero cleanly; when a log/brief target dir is unwritable, it falls back to `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/minsky-<id>.log` with a one-line warn and continues.
  - **Success**: `bin/minsky-run.sh` (and `bin/minsky` doctor) classify these three runtime failures into one-line, path-naming, recovery-hint messages (not raw errnos); a new bats suite asserts each branch.
  - **Pivot**: if the `/tmp` log fallback collides on multi-tenant hosts, scope it to `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/minsky-${USER}-<id>.log`; if the read-only-mount detection is over-defensive (hosts mount sub-paths read-only intentionally), demote that branch to detect-and-warn and let the operator's mkdir failure surface naturally.
  - **Measurement**: `bats tests/runtime-resilience.bats 2>&1 | grep -qE '0 failures' && grep -qE 'chmod u\+w|MINSKY_HOME' bin/minsky-run.sh`
  - **Anchor**: Beyer, Jones, Petoff, Murphy (eds.), *Site Reliability Engineering*, O'Reilly 2016, Ch. 6 (graceful degradation); Armstrong, *Making Reliable Distributed Systems in the Presence of Software Errors*, 2003 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary).
  - **Details**: (a) In `bin/minsky-run.sh`, upgrade the experiment-store `mkdir -p ... || INVARIANT FAIL` path (around the `ensure_*_dir` helper) to print the offending path + a recovery hint (`chmod u+w <path>` or set `MINSKY_HOME=<writable>`) before the non-zero return. (b) Wrap the brief/log file writes so an unwritable target dir falls back to `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/minsky-<id>.log` with a one-line warn and continues the iteration. (c) Add a pre-flight guard for the run target / openhands spawn shim: when missing or non-executable, emit a one-line message naming the path + the fix (`pnpm install`, `chmod +x`) and exit non-zero. (d) Add a `minsky daemon doctor` row reporting whether the state dir is writable (extend `scripts/bash-doctor-probes.sh`). (e) New `tests/runtime-resilience.bats` exercising each branch against a temp unwritable dir + a missing-target stub. (f) Cross-link in `novel/tick-loop/README.md`.
  - **Files**: `bin/minsky-run.sh` (three resilience branches), `bin/minsky` (doctor row wiring), `scripts/bash-doctor-probes.sh` (state-dir-writable probe), `tests/runtime-resilience.bats` (new), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (cross-link).
  - **Touches**: bin/minsky-run.sh, bin/minsky, scripts/bash-doctor-probes.sh, tests/runtime-resilience.bats, novel/tick-loop/README.md
  - **Acceptance**: (a) unwritable state dir → one-line path + recovery-hint message, clean non-zero exit; (b) unwritable log/brief dir → `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}` fallback + warn, iteration continues; (c) missing run target/shim → actionable one-line message; (d) `bats tests/runtime-resilience.bats` exits 0; (e) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.
  - **Composes-with**: `minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap` (sibling — same loud-fail-at-the-right-boundary discipline in the bash CLI).
- [ ] `minsky-claude-exhaustion-persisted-state` — slice 4 of self-healing: persist last claude hard-limit hit in `.minsky/state.json` so a fresh `minsky` startup detects exhaustion without relying on a token-too-small live probe
  - **ID**: minsky-claude-exhaustion-persisted-state
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — obsolete (test-cited; remove the test citation, then this block): All target files gone (novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts, llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts, daemon.ts, bin/minsky.mjs, bin/tick-loop.mjs deleted in Path A). No claude-vs
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, claude-exhaustion, dx
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens. It shouldn't have happened, it should have quickly detected that & switched to local model". Aggressiveness: detect + auto-fix safe ops (write to `.minsky/state.json` is INSIDE `.minsky/` so it's fair game per the operator's chosen aggressiveness).
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: The startup probe `claude --print "ping"` is a 1-token query; Anthropic's quota metering hits at the multi-K-token level (an iteration is typically 5-15K input tokens). When the operator's quota is exhausted, the 1-token probe can still return exit 0 — false-positive on `healthy`. The daemon then spawns claude on iteration 1, which fails with hard-limit; the existing per-iteration `decideProvider` logic correctly switches to local on iteration 2 — but the operator already saw iteration 1 spawn claude (the bug they reported). Plus, even if iteration 2 switches to local, that requires the local-LLM stack to already be installed; if it isn't (because `maybeBootstrapLocalLlm` skipped the bootstrap based on the false-positive probe), iteration 2 lands in `hold` mode. Pre-registration: post-fix, when `.minsky/state.json::last_claude_hard_limit.ts` is recent (within `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN` minutes; default 60), `minsky` startup SKIPS the live probe and goes directly to the local-LLM bootstrap path. The daemon writes this field whenever its iteration loop catches a hard-limit signal (via `isClaudeHardLimit(failure)`). Composes with: existing `decideProvider` (in-process per-iteration) + new persistence layer (cross-process / cross-restart).
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` exporting `readLastHardLimit(opts: { stateFilePath, readFileSyncFn, existsSyncFn, nowFn, ttlMs })` returning `{ exhausted: boolean, ageMs?, reason?, ts? }`; and `writeLastHardLimit(opts: { stateFilePath, readFileSyncFn, writeFileSyncFn, ts, reason })` that updates the state.json atomically (read → modify → write — same shape as setup.sh's ledger writes). (b) `bin/minsky.mjs::maybeBootstrapLocalLlm` consults `readLastHardLimit` BEFORE the live `probeClaude()` call. Recent → log `minsky: persisted hard-limit hit at <ts> (<N>m ago); skipping live probe and bootstrapping local-LLM` and proceed to bootstrap path. Stale → run probe as before. (c) Daemon spawn-strategy (`LlmProviderSpawnStrategy.spawn`) gets a new injected seam `persistHardLimit?: (failure) => Promise<void>` that's called when `isClaudeHardLimit(failure) === true`. Production wiring in `bin/tick-loop.mjs` sets it to a function that calls `writeLastHardLimit`. Test layer leaves it `undefined` (no-op). (d) `minsky --help` adds two new lines under "Operator escape hatches": `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred minsky` (force local immediately) and `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN=<N>` (configure persisted-state TTL). (e) `minsky doctor` adds a row "claude exhaustion (persisted)" showing GREEN ✓ when no recent hard-limit, YELLOW ⚠ with timestamp when recent. (f) Update `novel/tick-loop/README.md` slice 4 section + `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` cross-link.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts` (add `persistHardLimit` injected seam), `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts` (re-exports), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (wire read into maybeBootstrapLocalLlm + doctor row + --help), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire write seam in spawn strategy construction), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (slice 4 section), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (cross-link).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/README.md`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `readLastHardLimit` covering: state file absent, state file present + field absent, field present + within TTL, field present + stale, field present + corrupt JSON. Paired tests for `writeLastHardLimit` covering: state file absent (creates), state file present + field absent (adds), field present (overwrites). Live integration: (i) `echo '{"schema_version":"1","last_claude_hard_limit":{"ts":"<now>","reason":"test"}}' > .minsky/state.json && minsky` skips live probe and starts local-LLM bootstrap; (ii) `minsky doctor` shows YELLOW row "claude exhaustion (persisted)" with timestamp; (iii) `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN=5 minsky` honors the env override.
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, `echo '...' > .minsky/state.json && pnpm minsky 2>&1 | grep -c "persisted hard-limit"` returns ≥1. Test count delta: +8 paired tests (5 read + 3 write).
  - **Pivot**: if persisted-state false-positives (operator's quota DID reset but persisted state hasn't been cleared), the live probe runs after TTL anyway — so the worst case is one extra wall-clock hour on local-LLM. If that proves unacceptable, lower the TTL default or add a `--force-claude` operator override. If `state.json` write contention with other minsky processes (multiple workers) causes corruption, switch to per-worker state files (`.minsky/state-worker-<id>.json`). If the spawn strategy seam introduces test-time async surprises (race between in-process state and on-disk state), default the seam to in-process-only and expose the on-disk persistence as an opt-in flag.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens"). Slice 4 of self-healing trilogy. PRs #396/#398/#399 (slices 1-3 of self-healing). Rule #1 (don't reinvent — reuse the slice 1-3 pure-helper-with-paired-tests pattern). Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — the right boundary for "claude exhausted" is "skip claude and use local", not "spawn claude and let it fail"). Rule #9 (pre-registration). Composes with existing `LlmProviderSpawnStrategy` per-iteration logic. Sources: Beyer et al. (SRE) Ch. 6; Anthropic CLI docs on `claude --print` exit codes; Ries (Lean Startup) for build-measure-learn — persisted state IS the measurement layer.
  - **Risk**: low. Each new check is a `readFileSync` (sub-millisecond) on the existing `.minsky/state.json` file. Write is on the daemon's failure path (already an exceptional code path). No mutation outside `.minsky/`.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator live-run 2026-05-08 — "I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens. It shouldn't have happened, it should have quickly detected that & switched to local model". Root cause analysis: 1-token probe is below Anthropic's metering threshold; existing in-process per-iteration `decideProvider` correctly fires on iteration 2 but the user already saw iteration 1's wasted claude spawn.

- [ ] `minsky-cli-context-aware-ux` — `minsky` (no args) reads the machine's full context (worker state, daemon state, claude state, git state, queue state) and offers a single confirm-or-multi-select prompt for what to do next
  - **ID**: minsky-cli-context-aware-ux
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — obsolete (test-cited; remove the test citation, then this block): Targets deleted TS substrate (novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts, minsky-action-plan.ts, minsky-prompt.ts, bin/minsky.mjs). bin/minsky is now a bash shim; the 7-scenario prompt
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, ux, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Status**: in-progress — basic "smart auto-attach → watch" is SHIPPED (bin/minsky `Smart auto-attach` block, 2026-05-18). Operator running `minsky` (no args) in a folder now: (a) attaches to the existing daemon for that folder via `exec minsky watch`, OR (b) starts a new daemon + auto-installs launchd persistence + attaches. Remaining scope: the 7-scenario context-aware multi-select prompt (claude-exhausted-with-local-stack / queue-empty / WIP-needs-cleanup / git-dirty-cant-iterate / etc.) is still open. The simple two-state (running / not-running) auto-attach covers the minsky-on-itself case; the full multi-state prompt covers fresh checkouts, stuck WIP, and provider-exhausted states.
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)".
  - **Estimate**: 3d
  - **Hypothesis**: Today `minsky` (no args) collapses to "start-or-attach worker 0 with sane defaults". That's the right default for the dogfood-on-self loop, but not the right default for: a fresh checkout (no daemon ever ran, no `.minsky/state.json`), a machine that ran the daemon earlier and is mid-task (workers stopped between sessions), a machine where `main` advanced and the operator wants to merge / rebase before iterating, or a machine where claude has run dry. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky` (no args) reads ≤7 signals (workers running, daemon PID liveness, last iteration timestamp, claude probe state, local-LLM state, `git status` cleanliness, open daemon PR count + CONFLICTING count) and renders one of N pre-defined "scenarios" (clean-fresh-checkout / daemon-mid-iteration / claude-exhausted-with-local-stack / claude-exhausted-no-stack / WIP-needs-cleanup / git-dirty-cant-iterate / queue-empty). Each scenario carries a default action and a multi-select alternatives list. The operator confirms with `[Enter]` (default) or types a number to pick an alternative. Target: from `minsky` invocation to first action, ≤2 s p95 (the detection is fast; the prompt is human-time but not blocking). Operator-perceived UX: "I just type `minsky` and it tells me what to do next AND why".
  - **Details**: (a) New module `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts` exporting `gatherMinskyContext(opts: GatherOpts): Promise<MinskyContext>` — 7 parallel detection probes, each timeout-bounded at 500 ms. (b) Pure decision function `planMinskyAction(context: MinskyContext): MinskyActionPlan` returning `{ scenario, recommendedAction, alternatives }`. (c) Prompt module `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts` exporting `runInteractive(plan, opts: { stdin, stdout, isTty })` that handles `[Y/n]` confirm AND multi-select via numbered options (`1`/`2`/`3` keystrokes); on non-TTY (CI / launchd / piped), the recommended action runs without prompting (rule #6 — silence on non-interactive surfaces is correct, not failure). (d) `bin/minsky.mjs` no-args path becomes: `gatherMinskyContext` → `planMinskyAction` → `runInteractive` → execute the chosen action (which may delegate back to existing `runStartOrAttach`, `runLogs`, `runStop`, or new `runBootstrapLocalLlm`, `runMergeWipPrs`, etc.). (e) Snapshot tests for the 7 scenarios with synthetic context fixtures so the Markdown output stays stable.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.ts` (new pure decision), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (no-args path rewrite + back-compat for `minsky logs|stop|<id>`), `README.md` (retire the "Not a global CLI" disclaimer; add a "What `minsky` (no args) does" section).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `README.md`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each of the 7 scenarios with golden-file snapshots of the rendered prompt. Integration test: synthetic `.minsky/` directory representing each scenario, `minsky` non-interactive (`MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1`), assert the recommended action runs. Manual operator walkthrough: each of the 7 scenarios on a real machine produces an intuitive "yes, that's what I wanted" outcome (the soft acceptance criterion).
  - **Measurement**: `time minsky </dev/null >/dev/null 2>&1` p95 ≤2 s over 100 invocations (the detection layer's wall-clock budget). AND post-rollout: count of `minsky [<args>]` invocations where the operator types a positional argument vs no-args — the no-args fraction should rise to ≥60 % within 14 days (pre-rollout baseline: ~10 % since the no-args path is currently just "start worker 0").
  - **Pivot**: if the 7-scenario decision tree is too brittle (real machines hit 8th / 9th edge cases the table doesn't cover), retire the multi-select prompt and degrade to "list 5 actions, type the number" — preserves the context-aware detection but drops the "default action with confirm" UX. If detection is too slow (≥2 s p95), parallelise harder or retire individual probes (e.g., drop the `gh pr list` call which dominates wall-clock; keep only the local-state probes).
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `prompts` / `inquirer` / `enquirer` are industry-standard interactive-prompt libraries; pick whichever has the smallest dep footprint at decision time); rule #2 (Strategy boundary — `gatherMinskyContext` is pure over an injected probe seam; the prompt is the I/O); rule #6 (stay-alive — non-TTY mode runs the recommended action without prompting, so cron / launchd / CI never block on stdin); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD). Composes with `minsky-cli-auto-bootstrap-local-llm` (P0, queued) — the bootstrap is one of the recommended actions the prompt offers.
  - **Risk**: medium. Adding an interactive prompt to a CLI that historically ran unattended risks breaking the daemon's launchd / systemd surface (where stdin is closed). Mitigation: explicit non-interactive mode (`MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1` AND `process.stdout.isTTY === false`) where the recommended action runs without prompting. The launchd unit-files already pipe stdin from `/dev/null`, so the detection is automatic.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator request 2026-05-08 — "Overall I want minsky to be powerful and straightforward cli tool. I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)".

<!-- 9-hour monitoring window 2026-05-06 22:00 → 2026-05-07 ~07:30 found 4 minsky-loop bugs that lost throughput and required manual unblock. Filed below as P0 (operator directive 2026-05-07 — "use p0 for important things like minsky loop bugs"). They share the framing the operator articulated 2026-05-07: "monitor + unblock + file tasks so next time minsky unblocks itself" — i.e., the watchdog substrate that makes 10-worker mode safe. -->
- [ ] `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` — when daemon's PR fails CI, daemon automatically opens a fix commit on the same branch instead of noop-iterating
  - **ID**: daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — test-cited by scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs:202; remove that citation, then this block (or re-author). Substrate refs may be stale (novel/tick-loop deleted).
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, self-improvement, pick-next
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Pick-next**: yes (operator-flagged 2026-05-05 — supervisor should pick this up immediately after `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` ships).
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: Empirical observation 2026-05-05: with `cross-repo-ci-action` task block in TASKS.md (PR #167 open), the daemon iterated 80+ times producing brief refreshes / noops because the PR can't merge while CI fails, the task can't be removed while the PR is open, and the daemon won't fix CI on its own PR. **Deadlock pattern**. Fix: when the daemon detects its PR exists for the current task AND the PR has failing CI checks, the daemon iteration's brief becomes "fix CI failures on PR #N" instead of "redo the task". Operator never has to intervene; the daemon closes its own loop. Pre-registration: post-fix, time-from-PR-open-to-merge for daemon-authored PRs drops from "indefinite — operator must intervene" to "≤2 daemon iterations median".
  - **Details**: (a) In the daemon's task-pick step (right before claude --print), check if `gh pr list --head <branch>` returns an open PR for the current task ID's branch. (b) If yes AND the PR has failing CI checks, fetch the failure logs (`gh run view --log-failed <id>`) and pass them to claude --print as the brief: "Fix the failing CI checks on PR #N. Failure summary: <log excerpt>". (c) The daemon's claude pushes the fix commit; CI re-runs; next iteration checks again; loop until green or 3 retries. (d) After 3 retries, the daemon labels the PR `Blocked: daemon-stuck` and synthesises a new TASKS.md entry summarising what's blocked (operator-actionable). (e) Composes with `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` (above) — that gate cuts most failures at PR-open time; this gate handles the residue.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.ts` + tests (the decision function: open-PR-and-failing? → which-failure-class? → fix-brief), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.ts` + tests (the fix-iteration entry), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire-in).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for daemon-pr-state (no-pr / pr-clean / pr-failing / pr-3-retries-exhausted); integration test that opens a synthetic PR with a deliberate failure, runs one daemon iteration, asserts a fix commit landed.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot" --state closed --search "merged:>$(date -v-30d -u +%Y-%m-%d)" --json createdAt,closedAt --jq '[.[] | (((.closedAt|fromdate) - (.createdAt|fromdate)) / 60)] | sort | .[length/2|floor]'` (median minutes from PR open to merge for daemon PRs over rolling 30d) ≤ 240 (4h — accounts for human review on substantive changes; CI-fix-only iterations close in <30min).
  - **Pivot**: if the daemon's fix iteration takes >3 retries reliably (>20% of failing PRs), the failure classes the daemon faces aren't fixable by claude --print alone — pivot to a "human escalation" mode: after 1 retry, the daemon labels the PR `needs-operator` and stops iterating. Don't build infinite-retry — that wastes the budget without producing value.
  - **Anchor**: rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the boundary — the daemon's own PR is its boundary; a green CI is the contract); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6 (the operator-escape-hatch is `Blocked: daemon-stuck`); rule #9 (the 4h median is the pre-registered metric); empirical 2026-05-05 (PR #167's 80-iteration deadlock).
  - **Risk**: medium-high. The daemon could iterate destructively if its fix-brief is wrong (e.g., suppressing a lint instead of fixing the violation). Mitigation: the cap-3 retries + `Blocked: daemon-stuck` escalation; also, the in-tree pre-push lint stack catches obvious destructive changes.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 user request — "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself" + my analysis identified the deadlock. This is the second daemon self-improvement.

Replacements: 50-line `bin/check-budget.sh` shell, spec-only-in-mape-k-loop for prompt-optimizer.
  - **Status**: 3-of-5 done. `handoff-spec` + `bridges/omc-tasksmd` deleted in Phase 9 partial PR (this PR); `tui` source deleted in #794. - [ ] `minsky-repo-git-config-bare-misset` — `.git/config` on the operator's minsky checkout has `bare = true`, but the directory contains a working tree with active worktrees (`.git/worktrees/daemon-0-*`, `fix-ci-main`, `fleet-stability`, `minsky-bench`). Every `git status` from the main checkout fails with `fatal: this operation must be run in a work tree`. Daemon self-diagnose flagged it under `git-config-parseable` but proposed the wrong fix (`rm .git/index.lock` — index lock is not the issue). Real fix: one-line `bare = false`. The self-diagnose handler should detect `bare = true` AND working files coexisting, propose the correct fix
  - **ID**: minsky-repo-git-config-bare-misset
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Competitive-goal**: drives `mttr-self-heal` p95 toward <5min (M1.13) — competitors' self-diagnose surfaces (Devin's `diagnose`, Cursor's health-check) don't propose actionable fixes for unusual git states; Minsky's self-diagnose that flags `bare=true with worktrees` AND proposes `git config core.bare false` is a measurable diagnose-vs-suggest quality win.
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m1, m1-1, observed-2026-05-26, self-diagnose-misdirection
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-26 — every iteration's self-diagnose emits `git status failed (...fatal: this operation must be run in a work tree)`. Confirmed via `cat <minsky-repo>/.git/config` → `[core] bare = true`. `.git/worktrees/` shows 5 active worktrees (4 daemon-spawned + 3 operator). The daemon's self-diagnose suggested `rm .git/index.lock` (the index isn't locked — `ls .git` shows no `index.lock`). Real fix: flip `bare = false` (or remove the line). Tracked to a likely accidental `git init --bare` or similar tool misconfig at some point in the repo's history.
  - **Hypothesis**: extend the self-diagnose handler in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/daemon.ts` (or wherever `git-config-parseable` is computed) — when `git status` fails with `fatal: this operation must be run in a work tree`, ALSO probe `git config core.bare` and `ls .git/worktrees/`. If both `bare = true` AND worktree-entries exist, suggest `git config core.bare false` instead of the index-lock fix. The combination is mechanically diagnostic. Falsifiable: simulate the bug on a test fixture (`git init && git config core.bare true && touch a.txt`), run the daemon's self-diagnose, assert the suggested fix is the bare flip — not the index lock.
  - **Success**: (1) Self-diagnose detects bare-misset and proposes the correct fix string; (2) Test fixture in `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/self-diagnose-bare-misset.test.mjs` (new) reproduces both detection AND correct suggestion; (3) Operator runs the suggested `git config core.bare false`, `git status` works, daemon iteration completes normally.
  - **Pivot**: if detecting `bare = true` is too fragile (different git versions emit slightly different error messages), gate the new diagnostic behind a `MINSKY_SELF_DIAGNOSE_BARE_DETECTION=1` env var. Threshold: ≥1 false-positive ("flagged bare-misset when actually a different issue") within 7 days of rollout.
  - **Measurement**: `cd <minsky-repo> && git status --short 2>&1 | head -1 | awk '/fatal/ {print "FAIL"} !/fatal/ {print "PASS"}'`
  - **Anchor**: Rule #1 (loud-crash > silent failure — the daemon DOES emit a self-diagnose finding, but the suggested fix is wrong, so the operator follows the misleading advice and the bug persists). Rule #17 (proactive healing — once the correct fix is detected, the next step is auto-applying it; this task only fixes the diagnosis layer, auto-apply is a follow-up).
  - **Details**: (a) Find the self-diagnose handler that emits `git-config-parseable`. (b) After confirming `git status` fails, probe `git config core.bare` (read-only). (c) If `true`, probe `ls -d .git/worktrees/* 2>/dev/null` for active worktrees. (d) If both signals match, suggest `git config core.bare false` instead of the index-lock fix. (e) Paired tests for: bare=false (no false positive), bare=true with no worktrees (true bare repo — different fix needed), bare=true with worktrees (the bug case — propose correct fix). (f) Don't auto-apply the fix yet — that's a follow-up task once the detection is proven stable.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/daemon.ts` (extend self-diagnose handler — locate via `grep -n git-config-parseable`), `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/self-diagnose-bare-misset.test.mjs` (new — paired tests with fixture worktrees), `~/.minsky/daemon.log` (verify after rollout — new suggestedFix string visible).
  - **Touches**: novel/cross-repo-runner/src/daemon.ts,novel/cross-repo-runner/test/self-diagnose-bare-misset.test.mjs
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner/test/self-diagnose-bare-misset.test.mjs` passes; (2) `pnpm typecheck` clean; (3) Operator runs `cat <minsky-repo>/.git/config | grep bare` → sees `bare = true` (today's state); runs `git config core.bare false`; runs `git status` → works; the next iteration's self-diagnose drops the finding (no longer fires); (4) When run against a fresh bare-misset fixture, the daemon's self-diagnose emits a suggestedFix containing `git config core.bare false`.

     `ghi-task-backend-contract`. Origin: managed-host RFC `github-issues-task-tracking`. -->

  - **ID**: ghi-task-source-github-issues-impl

  - **Status**: obsolete — blocked by ghi-task-source-interface which was superseded by Path A aggressive cut (2026-05-24). Re-scope this task if GitHub Issues task backend is still needed for the Python picker (`scripts/pick_task.py`).
  - **Touches**: <none>
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: moves `task-backend-coverage` from TASKS.md-only to TASKS.md + github-issues — the daemon can now run an indefinite improvement loop on a repo whose queue is GitHub Issues, which is the prerequisite for driving managed-host after its migration.
  - **Hypothesis**: A GitHub-Issues implementation of the `TaskSource` port — listing open issues on the host's org Project ordered by the Priority field, claiming by self-assigning the daemon's agent identity, and closing via the merged PR's `Closes #N` — lets the existing host loop drive an issues-backed repo with no host-loop changes.
  - **Success**: `task-source.github-issues.ts` implements all four port verbs against `gh`/Projects v2, has a `selfTest()` that round-trips a fixture issue (create → list → claim → close), and an integration test drives the four verbs against a fixture repo; priority ordering matches the P0→P3 walk.

  - **Anchor**: GitHub docs "Linking a pull request to an issue" (default-branch close keywords) + "Using the built-in automations" (Projects v2 "PR merged → Done"), GHES 3.18.4 (verified on a GitHub Enterprise host); Cockburn Ports & Adapters 2005.
  - **Details**: Implement the four verbs: `listOpenTasks` = `gh issue list` on the host's Project filtered to open + ordered by Priority (from the agentbrew contract descriptor); `claim` = `gh issue edit --add-assignee <agentId>`; `close` is implicit via the agent's merged PR carrying `Closes #N` (the adapter's `close` is a safety net / no-op verify); `getTask` = `gh issue view --json`. Provide `selfTest()`. Reuse agentbrew's `gh-issues` helper shape where practical (don't duplicate the rate-limit/scope logic — cite it).
  - **Files**: `novel/adapters/task-source.github-issues.ts` (new), `novel/adapters/task-source.github-issues.test.ts` (new), `novel/adapters/task-source.github-issues.selftest.mjs` (new), `test/integration/task-source-github-issues-fixture.test.ts` (new), `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` (note the second adapter).

- [ ] `lint-stack-audit-post-openhands-wrap` — audit + delete lint stages redundant with OpenHands' output; target 53 → 20 stages
  - **ID**: lint-stack-audit-post-openhands-wrap
  - **Tags**: p1, strategic, reshape, observed-2026-05-22, codebase-reduction, external-dep-needed
  - **Blocked**: needs-openhands-wrap-shipped (depends on `add-openhands-as-pluggable-backend` landing first)
  - **Milestone**: M2
  - **Competitive-goal**: closes the "70K LOC for 1 operator is unsustainable" math from the 2026-05-22 strategic review. The lint stack is 53K LOC (~75% of the codebase). Many stages exist because Minsky couldn't trust spawned agents (Claude/Devin/Aider) to do the right thing. Post-OpenHands-wrap, the agent has higher single-task quality (65.8% SWE-bench, critic + best-of-N) and inherits OpenHands' own quality gates. Many Minsky lint stages become redundant. Deleting them is the largest single lever for getting Minsky to the 10K-LOC sustainable footprint (Path C of the strategic review).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (the orchestrator that lists the 53 stages), each `scripts/check-*.mjs` lint script that becomes redundant (delete + remove from the stack), `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (CI jobs that mirror local lints — delete in lockstep), `AGENTS.md` § rule references (some constitutional rules may need re-anchoring to surviving lints), `docs/PRACTICES.md` (the lint-stack documentation), `vision.md` rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — the surviving lint set must still cover the 17 constitutional rules with at least 1 lint each).
  - **Details**: 2026-05-22 strategic review (docs/strategic-review-2026-05-22-continue-or-wrap-more.md § "What's wrapped vs what stays Minsky") identified lint-stack pruning as the largest deletion target. Procedure: (a) for each of the 53 pre-pr-lint stages, write a 1-sentence "why does this exist?" justification, (b) check whether OpenHands' output already satisfies the invariant the lint guards against (e.g., `brief-pr-instructions` checks the PR body has a "## Why this is needed" section — OpenHands' PR generator likely produces this by default; verify), (c) for each redundant lint, delete the script + remove from the stack + remove the CI job, (d) for each non-redundant lint, document WHY it survives (so future audits don't re-question), (e) re-run pre-pr-lint --stage=full on 3 fixture PRs to confirm the slim stack catches the same violation set the full stack did. Target output: 53 → 20 stages, with a documented justification table for the surviving 20.
  - **Hypothesis**: at least 25 of the 53 pre-pr-lint stages are belt-and-braces for failure modes OpenHands' agent doesn't produce. Aggressive deletion saves ~25K LOC of script code + frees the operator from maintaining lints that catch zero violations in practice.
  - **Success**: `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` shows ≤20 stages green; LOC of `scripts/check-*.mjs` files drops by ≥25K; the constitutional-rule coverage (each of 17 rules → ≥1 deterministic lint) is preserved in the surviving stack; integration test runs the slim stack against the 10 most-recent merged PRs and confirms zero false-positives.
  - **Pivot**: if the audit reveals only ~5 stages are redundant, the deletion strategy is wrong — most lints catch real Minsky-specific violations that OpenHands doesn't address. Revisit Path C; consider whether constitution-as-CI is doing more work than the strategic review credited it for.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full 2>&1 | grep -c '\[ok\]'` returns ≤20; `wc -l scripts/check-*.mjs | tail -1` shows ≥25K LOC reduction vs baseline; `node scripts/audit-constitutional-rule-coverage.mjs` (new — verifies each rule has ≥1 lint).
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent — OpenHands ships quality gates we'd otherwise build); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — surviving lints must still cover all 17 rules); docs/strategic-review-2026-05-22-continue-or-wrap-more.md § "Path C — Continue, but RESHAPE"; competitors/openhands.md § "What we keep" — the wrap analysis explicitly noted Minsky owns the constitution layer; this task is the reshape of HOW Minsky owns it (fewer lints, sharper coverage).

  - **ID**: multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec

  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m2, multi-persona, novel-package, handoffs

Each persona writes its handoff on exit; the next persona reads it on start. Validation at the schema level catches the most common bug (persona writes the wrong nextPersona or omits status).
  - **Success**: a 5-persona pipeline (researcher → planner → developer → QA → reviewer) runs end-to-end against a single fixture task; each handoff file validates against the schema; the pipeline ends with a complete reviewer-produced PR description. Pipeline-completion rate ≥80% over the first 20 production runs.

  - **Anchor**: Hewitt 1973 Actor Model (IJCAI — independent actors communicate via messages) composed with Hayes-Roth 1985 Blackboard (specialists writing to a shared workspace). The handoff file IS the message; the blackboard IS the `.minsky/handoffs/<task-id>/` directory.
  - **Details**: (1) Finalise the JSON schema at `novel/handoff-spec/schema.json`. (2) Ship `novel/handoff-spec/src/{validate,write,read}.ts` with paired tests. (3) Wire into `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` so pipeline-tagged tasks fan out the personas. (4) Per-persona budget caps in config. (5) Failure mode: if any persona fails, the pipeline files `pipeline-failed-<task>-<persona>` and stops; the operator unblocks manually.
  - **Files**: `novel/handoff-spec/schema.json` (new), `novel/handoff-spec/src/{validate,write,read}.ts` (new), sibling tests, `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (wire pipeline branch), `user-stories/008-per-task-backend-and-personas.test.ts` (activate the skipped pipeline test).
  - **Touches**: novel/handoff-spec/, novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts, user-stories/008-*.test.ts
  - **Acceptance**: pipeline completes for ≥80% of 20 fixture runs; per-persona handoff files validate; the reviewer-produced PR description is non-empty and references the prior personas' outputs.
  - **Risk**: medium. Multi-persona introduces handoff-spec brittleness (each persona's idea of "done" may differ). Mitigation: the schema's `status` enum is the contract; an invalid status fails fast.
  - **Note**: blocked on nothing; this is M2 net-new work. The user-story 008's `it.skip` test activates against this implementation.

- [ ] `claude-agents-deep-integration` — minsky's persona library (researcher, manager, developer, qa-engineer, reviewer, alternatives-analyst, indie-hacker, growth-hacker, strategist, agent-improver, user, pipeline-runner) is exposed as Claude Code sub-agents under `.claude/agents/*.md` so the operator can invoke them via `/agents` AND the M2 multi-persona pipeline executes through Claude's native sub-agent surface instead of shelling out to a separate CLI subprocess per persona
  - **ID**: claude-agents-deep-integration
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Spec inputs absent (orchestrator skills, persona-spawner adapter); success needs live /agents session test
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m2, integration, claude, personas, handoffs, observed-2026-05-20
  - **Milestone**: M2
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 — "Let's ensure that deep integration with claude's /agents command is P1 task". Today minsky ships personas as `.claude/skills/orchestrator-*` markdown (operator-facing skills the human can read) AND as `subagent_*` profiles in the global agentbrew (the `subagent_explore` / `subagent_general` profiles I use via `run_subagent`). Neither is the Claude Code `.claude/agents/*.md` sub-agent format — so the operator cannot type `/agents` in their Claude session and see minsky's persona library. The personas exist conceptually in three formats but none are the canonical one Claude Code reads.
  - **Hypothesis**: Claude Code reads sub-agent definitions from `.claude/agents/*.md` with YAML frontmatter (`name`, `description`, `tools`, `model`). Generating these files from the existing `.claude/skills/orchestrator-*/SKILL.md` source (which already encodes the persona's identity, scope, tool-access posture, and trigger phrases) is a deterministic transformation. Once present, two payoffs land: (a) the operator can `/agents` to discover and invoke minsky's persona library from their own Claude session — "use the researcher agent to investigate X" routes through Claude's native sub-agent invocation; (b) when minsky's tick-loop spawns a multi-persona pipeline (task `multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec`), each persona is invoked via Claude's Task tool (sub-agent dispatch) instead of via a separate `claude --print --model ...` subprocess — same isolation, half the per-invocation overhead (no fresh process startup, no `~/.claude` re-bootstrap), and the handoff files at `.minsky/handoffs/<task-id>/` stay the inter-persona protocol.
  - **Success**: (1) `ls .claude/agents/*.md` lists ≥7 personas (researcher, manager, alternatives-analyst, developer, qa-engineer, reviewer, agent-improver — the core orchestrator pipeline) — count via `find .claude/agents -name "*.md" -type f | wc -l` ≥7. (2) Operator runs `claude` in the minsky repo, types `/agents`, sees the personas — manually verified end-to-end. (3) "Use the researcher agent to investigate the test-coverage gap" spawns a Claude sub-agent that reads the researcher persona's instructions; the sub-agent produces output that conforms to the researcher's handoff format (validated against `novel/handoff-spec/schema.json`). (4) The multi-persona pipeline test (`user-stories/008-per-task-backend-and-personas.test.ts`'s skipped pipeline case) activates and passes when this task ships AND `multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec` ships — both together enable the M2 pipeline path. (5) `.claude/agents/*.md` regenerates idempotently from `scripts/generate-claude-agents.mjs` — re-running the script with no source changes produces a zero-diff git status.
  - **Pivot**: if Claude Code's sub-agent contract is too restrictive to encode the full minsky persona surface — specifically the per-persona budget caps (rule #15), the handoff-file output contract (`.minsky/handoffs/<task-id>/<persona>-<iso-ts>.md`), or the failure-mode boundary (a failed persona files `pipeline-failed-<task>-<persona>` and stops the pipeline) — abandon the deep integration and ship a thin discovery wrapper instead: `.claude/agents/*.md` files that contain only `name` + `description` + a one-line directive "the actual implementation runs as a minsky subprocess; this entry exists so `/agents` discovery surfaces the library". Threshold for pivot: ≥2 of the 5 success criteria above cannot be met within the Claude sub-agent surface after 2 implementation attempts.
  - **Measurement**: (a) `find .claude/agents -name "*.md" -type f | wc -l` returns ≥7. (b) `node scripts/validate-claude-agents.mjs` (new) parses each `.claude/agents/*.md`, verifies YAML frontmatter conforms to Claude Code's documented schema (name, description, tools, model — case-sensitive field names per the public docs), and exits 0. (c) `node scripts/generate-claude-agents.mjs --dry-run` produces no diff against the committed files (idempotency). (d) The pipeline integration test: `pnpm vitest run user-stories/008-per-task-backend-and-personas.test.ts --reporter=json | jq -e '.numFailedTests == 0 and (.testResults[] | .assertionResults[] | select(.title | contains("pipeline"))) | length >= 3'` — ≥3 pipeline-named test cases pass. (e) End-to-end manual verification documented in `docs/claude-agents.md` Quickstart section.
  - **Anchor**: Claude Code documentation on sub-agents (`docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/claude-code/sub-agents` — the `.claude/agents/*.md` format spec) composed with the actor-model pattern (Hewitt 1973, IJCAI — independent actors communicate via messages; sub-agents ARE actors, the Task tool IS the message dispatch) and the adapter pattern (rule #2 — Claude /agents is the external surface, `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/` is the existing adapter that ALREADY wraps persona invocation; this task adds a new implementation behind the same interface that targets Claude /agents instead of subprocess CLI). The dependency-as-adapter discipline keeps `multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec` agnostic of WHICH dispatch substrate routes the personas.
  - **Details**: (1) **Inventory step** — list every persona currently encoded somewhere in the minsky distribution. Sources: `.claude/skills/orchestrator-*/SKILL.md` (canonical persona definitions), the `subagent_*` profile descriptions in `~/.agents/profiles/` (operational scope-and-tools), and the personas mentioned in `vision.md § "Orchestrator personas"` (intent + literature anchors). Cross-reference these three into a single canonical-persona table at `novel/persona-registry/canonical.md`. (2) **Schema-pinning** — author a Claude-Code-sub-agent-compatible YAML frontmatter schema at `novel/persona-registry/claude-agent-schema.json`. Required fields per the public Claude Code docs: `name` (kebab-case, `^[a-z][a-z0-9-]+$`), `description` (one-line invocation hint), `tools` (allowlist; `*` for full), `model` (`sonnet`, `opus`, etc.). Allowed extension keys: `minsky.budgetMs`, `minsky.handoffFormat`, `minsky.failureMode` — namespaced so Claude Code ignores them while minsky's pipeline reads them. (3) **Generator** — `scripts/generate-claude-agents.mjs` (new) reads every `.claude/skills/orchestrator-*/SKILL.md`, parses its frontmatter + body, applies the schema, and writes the resulting `.claude/agents/<persona>.md`. Idempotent: re-running with no source changes is a no-op. (4) **Validator** — `scripts/validate-claude-agents.mjs` (new) checks every `.claude/agents/*.md` against the schema; wired into pre-pr-lint as a fast-stage check (`claude-agents-schema`). (5) **Pipeline-side integration** — `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/src/claude-agent.ts` (new, sibling to the existing subprocess-CLI implementation `process-spawn.ts`) dispatches a persona via Claude's Task tool when the runtime detects it's executing inside a Claude session (env var `CLAUDECODE=1` or equivalent). The choice between subprocess and Task-tool dispatch lives in `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/src/strategy.ts`, defaulting to subprocess when no Claude session is detected and to Task-tool when one is. (6) **Hot reload** — the daemon's next iteration reads `.claude/agents/*.md` fresh on each persona invocation; no restart needed. Edits to a persona file land in the next pipeline. (7) **Docs** — `docs/claude-agents.md` (new) documents the persona library, how to add a new one, how the operator invokes `/agents`, and the pipeline integration.
  - **Files**: `.claude/agents/researcher.md` (new), `.claude/agents/manager.md` (new), `.claude/agents/alternatives-analyst.md` (new), `.claude/agents/developer.md` (new), `.claude/agents/qa-engineer.md` (new), `.claude/agents/reviewer.md` (new), `.claude/agents/agent-improver.md` (new) — plus optional `pipeline-runner.md`, `indie-hacker.md`, `growth-hacker.md`, `user.md`, `strategist.md` if scope permits in slice 1; `novel/persona-registry/canonical.md` (new), `novel/persona-registry/claude-agent-schema.json` (new); `scripts/generate-claude-agents.mjs` (new), `scripts/generate-claude-agents.test.mjs` (new), `scripts/validate-claude-agents.mjs` (new), `scripts/validate-claude-agents.test.mjs` (new); `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/src/claude-agent.ts` (new), `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/src/strategy.ts` (modify to switch on runtime detection), `novel/adapters/persona-spawner/src/strategy.test.ts` (extend); `docs/claude-agents.md` (new); `vision.md` (add row to Pattern conformance index — adapter pattern, claude-agent dispatch); `README.md` (add `## More` link to `docs/claude-agents.md`); `user-stories/008-per-task-backend-and-personas.test.ts` (activate the skipped pipeline test case).
  - **Touches**: .claude/agents/, novel/persona-registry/, novel/adapters/persona-spawner/, scripts/{generate,validate}-claude-agents.mjs, docs/claude-agents.md
  - **Acceptance**: (1) Measurement criteria (a)-(d) above all pass. (2) The skipped pipeline test in `user-stories/008-*.test.ts` activates and passes (uses `describe.skipIf(!process.env.MINSKY_CLAUDE_AGENTS_ENABLED)` until the substrate ships). (3) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` passes — the new `claude-agents-schema` lint catches malformed frontmatter at PR-time. (4) Operator-side smoke: run `claude` in a fresh shell in the minsky repo, type `/agents`, manually confirm the persona library appears. Document the smoke procedure in `docs/claude-agents.md` Quickstart. (5) Rule-#10 (deterministic enforcement): the generator + validator are deterministic; re-running produces zero diff on a no-change source.
  - **Risk**: medium. The Claude Code sub-agent schema is documented but evolving; a future minor version may break the generator. Mitigation: pin to the documented schema version + version the schema file (`schema_version: 1` in YAML frontmatter); the validator's first check is the schema_version, so a future Claude Code update that changes the schema fails LOUDLY at lint-time rather than silently. Secondary risk: persona-tool-access posture must match Claude Code's `tools:` allowlist semantics — research persona allowed `read,grep,glob` but blocked `edit,write`; developer persona allowed full toolbox; reviewer allowed `read` only. Mis-specifying the allowlist defeats the security boundary (rule #13). Mitigation: each persona's `tools:` list is reviewed in PR comments and matches the documented persona scope.
  - **Note**: composes with `multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec` (the handoff format that personas read/write) and `motivation-bullet-test-coverage-completion` (story 008's `it.skip` cases activate against this implementation). Order: `multi-persona-pipeline-handoff-spec` ships first (the handoff substrate); this task ships second (the dispatch substrate); the M2 pipeline becomes live when both land. Optional follow-up: P2 `claude-agents-marketplace-publication` — once the persona library is canonicalised under `.claude/agents/`, consider publishing the library as a stand-alone npm package (`@minsky/claude-personas`) so other repos can install minsky's persona library without installing minsky itself.

- [ ] `minsky-npx-install-and-run` — `npx minsky` (no subcommand, no prior install) should both INSTALL minsky on the machine AND start a daemon iteration in a single command, so a new operator's literal first interaction is one shell line
  - **ID**: minsky-npx-install-and-run
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m1, ux, install, distribution, operator-directive, observed-2026-05-20
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 reviewing README — "Add a P1 task to make it install+runnable with a super simple command eg with npx". Today the install path is `git clone + cd + pnpm install + minsky`. The existing P0 `minsky-init-one-command-bootstrap` covers `npx minsky init` (sets up the sidecar) but leaves the operator to run `minsky` separately as a second command. The simpler operator-mental-model is: type ONE line in your shell, get a running iteration.
  - **Hypothesis**: publish minsky to npm as `@minsky/cli` (or just `minsky`, if the name's available) with a `bin` entry pointing at the existing `bin/minsky`. `npx minsky` (no subcommand) detects whether `~/.minsky/config.json` exists: if not, runs the `init` flow first (interactive choices: cwd as default_host, claude/devin/aider preference, model tier), then drops into the normal start-or-attach behaviour. If config exists, behaves identically to a local `minsky` invocation. Post-fix, a new operator runs ONE command (`npx minsky`) on a fresh macOS / Ubuntu box with Node 20 and is in a live iteration within ≤3 min — beating the current 10+ min clone-and-configure flow AND beating every OSS competitor's install path (Aider's pip install, OpenHands' Docker setup, SWE-agent's conda dance).
  - **Success**: (1) `npx -y minsky` on a fresh macOS VM with only Node 20 installed reaches "live iteration in progress" within 3 min (90th percentile). (2) Same on Ubuntu 24.04 VM. (3) `npx minsky --version` prints the published version without side-effects (probe-mode for scripts). (4) The published tarball is ≤5 MB compressed (npm convention; avoid heavy deps). (5) `npm uninstall -g minsky` or `npx minsky uninstall` (composing with the in-flight `minsky-uninstall-one-command-with-stop` P0) leaves zero residue.
  - **Pivot**: if npm publication blocks on a name conflict (`minsky` is taken by some other package), publish as `@minsky/cli` and document `npx @minsky/cli` as the canonical command. If `npx` startup latency is >10 s (cold cache, slow CI runner) the operator perceives the command as broken — pivot to `brew install minsky` (macOS) AND `curl -fsSL https://minsky.dev/install | sh` (universal) as primary, with `npx` as a backup. Threshold for pivot: 3 operators in 30 days report "I thought npx hung".
  - **Measurement**: `time npx -y minsky </dev/null` on a fresh VM with cold npm cache prints wall-clock ≤180s; `node_modules/.npm/_cacache` is sized ≤50 MB after the install (no surprise bloat); `pgrep -f cross-repo-runner` returns a non-empty PID list within 60s of npx completing.
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent — npm is the universal Node distribution channel); existing P0 `minsky-init-one-command-bootstrap` (composes with this — init is the prereq); Forsgren/Humble/Kim *Accelerate* 2018 (lead time — install IS the first lead-time metric); Krug *Don't Make Me Think* 2014 (one obvious path).
  - **Details**: (a) Add `bin` entry to root `package.json` pointing at `bin/minsky`. (b) Add `"files": ["bin/", "novel/", "scripts/", "lefthook.yml", "package.json"]` to limit the published tarball (exclude tests, fixtures, .minsky/, etc.). (c) `bin/minsky` already detects "no daemon → init + start"; add an "is this an npx invocation?" probe (env var `npm_lifecycle_event` or `npm_config_user_agent` — both set by npx) and prepend the `init` flow when (i) npx, AND (ii) no `~/.minsky/config.json`, AND (iii) interactive TTY. (d) Publish via `pnpm publish --access=public` from CI on tagged releases (v0.1.0+). (e) Test the published tarball end-to-end via `pnpm pack` + `npm install` in a clean Docker container; assert `minsky --version` works.
  - **Files**: `package.json` (`bin`, `files`, `version` fields), `bin/minsky` (npx-detection branch in the smart-attach block), `.github/workflows/release.yml` (new — npm publish on tag), `test/integration/npx-install.test.ts` (new — Docker-based fresh-install smoke).
  - **Touches**: `package.json`, `bin/minsky`, `.github/workflows/release.yml`, `test/integration/npx-install.test.ts`, `README.md`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) The published `minsky` package on npmjs.com has version ≥0.1.0 and `npx -y minsky` returns "live iteration in progress" on a fresh `node:20-bookworm` Docker container within 3 min. (2) README's Getting Started leads with `npx minsky` as the install line; the current `git clone + pnpm install` flow drops to a "Contributor setup" subsection. (3) `npm view minsky` shows the package size ≤5 MB. (4) Reverse path verified: `npx minsky uninstall` removes the runtime cleanly.
  - **Risk**: medium. npm publication requires the name to be free; npx startup is variable depending on the operator's npm cache; multi-platform launchd / systemd setup inside an npx-installed CLI is more complex than a local-clone install (the published tarball has to ship the distribution unit files but install them only on opt-in). Mitigation: paired Docker integration test for fresh-install; npm name reservation as a one-time admin step.
  - **Note**: depends on P0 `minsky-init-one-command-bootstrap` shipping first (init flow). Composes with P0 `minsky-uninstall-one-command-with-stop` (the symmetric reverse path).

- [ ] `pre-push-hook-stays-fast` — the lefthook `pre-push` step must stay under ~10s wall-clock; today the fix landed (`--stage=fast`), the policy needs a deterministic CI lint so a future PR can't silently regress
  - **ID**: pre-push-hook-stays-fast
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m1, rule-10, rule-11, dx, ci, feedback-loop, observed-2026-05-20
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-20 — "Hmm why did pre push take so long? I expected push to happen in like a second". `pre-push` ran `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` which invokes vitest (~35s for the 3,135-test suite); total wall-clock ~40s. Fixed in the same PR by switching to `--stage=fast` (~5-7s). Without a CI lint guarding the fast-stage choice, the next PR that touches `lefthook.yml` could silently revert and re-introduce the 35s tax on every developer push.
  - **Hypothesis**: ship `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.mjs` (rule-#10 deterministic lint) that asserts `lefthook.yml` `pre-push.commands.pre-pr-lint.run` ends with `--stage=fast` OR an explicitly-justified equivalent (`--stage=<custom-fast-subset>`). Hard-fail any PR whose lefthook.yml lacks the `--stage=fast` flag. Wire into the CI / `pre-pr-lint` stack so the lint runs on EVERY PR. Post-fix, the same operator complaint never recurs because the lint blocks the regression at PR time.
  - **Success**: (1) `node scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.mjs` exits 0 on the current `lefthook.yml`. (2) A synthetic test fixture where `pre-push.commands.pre-pr-lint.run` contains `--stage=full` makes the script exit 1 with `pre-push must use --stage=fast (current: --stage=full); see TASKS.md pre-push-hook-stays-fast`. (3) Paired vitest unit tests cover both shapes + the missing-`pre-push`-block case. (4) The lint is wired into `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` manifest so `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exercises it.
  - **Pivot**: if a future operator argues a slower pre-push is worth it (e.g., the gate-merge becomes unavailable on some platforms), gate the lint behind an `ALLOW_SLOW_PRE_PUSH=1` env var in `lefthook.yml` AND require a PR-body justification line `<!-- rule-10: pre-push-slow-justified: <reason> -->` (same shape as rule-3-doc-first's deferral marker). Don't loosen the default.
  - **Measurement**: `time git push origin <feature-branch>` on a clean tree should print ≤10s wall-clock (excluding network); empirically verified at 5-7s after this PR. `grep -c "stage=full" lefthook.yml` returns 0; the new script's CI invocation runs in <100ms.
  - **Anchor**: rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — `vision.md` § 10: every constitutional rule must be enforced by a deterministic CI check, not by "the agent will remember"); rule #11 (no flaky load-bearing gates — `vision.md` § "Constitutional rules" entry 11: pre-push is a load-bearing gate and a slow one is a flaky one in the operator-experience sense); Forsgren/Humble/Kim *Accelerate* 2018 (lead time + tight feedback loops are the most-correlated practice with high-performing teams).
  - **Details**: (a) Add `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.mjs` — pure parser over `lefthook.yml` + assertion that `pre-push.commands.pre-pr-lint.run` contains the substring `--stage=fast`. YAML parse via `js-yaml` (already a dep) OR a hand-rolled regex over the `run:` line (single source of truth: the line above the `run:` MUST be the `pre-pr-lint:` key). (b) Paired tests in `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.test.mjs` covering 5 shapes: current valid, `--stage=full` (rejected), missing `pre-push` block (rejected with actionable message), nested under wrong key (rejected), opt-out via `ALLOW_SLOW_PRE_PUSH=1` env var (accepted with one-line warning). (c) Wire into `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` STACK_MANIFEST so it runs in both `--stage=fast` and `--stage=full`. (d) CI parity row in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (when GHA is re-enabled) AND in the consolidated `pre-pr-lint` job. (e) Document the policy in `vision.md` § Pattern conformance index with a new row.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.mjs` (new), `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.test.mjs` (new), `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (add to manifest), `vision.md` (pattern conformance index row), `lefthook.yml` (already fixed in this PR — the lint exists to lock it in).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.mjs`, `scripts/check-pre-push-hook-fast.test.mjs`, `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs`, `vision.md`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` runs the new lint and reports `[ok] pre-push-hook-stays-fast`. (2) A synthetic PR that reverts `lefthook.yml` to `--stage=full` is blocked by the lint with the actionable message above. (3) `time git push` on a feature branch with one trivial commit completes in ≤10s wall-clock on the operator's box.
  - **Risk**: low. One pure script + paired tests + manifest wiring + one pattern-conformance row. No code path changes — the lint adds a gate, doesn't change runtime behaviour.
  - **Note**: composes with `commit-hook-chain-node-version-and-platform-resilience` (the existing P0 about commit hooks breaking quietly) — both are feedback-loop hygiene tasks.
