- [ ] `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` — launch N non-conflicting Minsky workers on the same repo via per-run worktree/lock/branch namespacing + pre-spawn task-claim arbitration
  - **ID**: daemon-parallel-worktree-launch
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — PR #1142 closed (branch kept): own acceptance test minsky-run.bats:230 (sibling-claim skip) passes in worktree, fails in CI — O_EXCL claim-gate race needs deterministic fix.
  - **Tags**: p0, supervisor, throughput, parallel, worktree, follow-up
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: raises merged-PR/day throughput by fanning out N isolated workers on one repo — the core autonomy-throughput metric Minsky competes on vs single-stream agents.
  - **Hypothesis**: The host walker (`bin/minsky-run.sh`) iterates serially. With N workers each owning a unique `deriveRunNamespace` worktree/lock/branch and a `deriveClaimKey`-arbitrated task, throughput multiplies up to the API ceiling; measured by merged-PR/day rising ≥1.5x the serial baseline at N=3 with zero claim collisions.
  - **Success**: at N=3, `scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs` reports 0 namespace collisions across ≥100 concurrent runs AND `countNamespaceCollisions` returns all-zero for the spawned set.
  - **Pivot**: if N=3 yields <1.2x serial-baseline merged-PR/day OR collisions >0 per 100 runs, drop to N=2 and gate on the API concurrency ceiling rather than adding workers.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs --json | node -e 'let s="";process.stdin.on("data",d=>s+=d).on("end",()=>{const j=JSON.parse(s);process.exit(j.collisions===0?0:1)})'`
  - **Anchor**: Lamport, "A New Solution of Dijkstra's Concurrent Programming Problem", CACM 1974 (mutual exclusion via uniquely-keyed locks); Leach/Mealling/Salz, RFC 4122 §4.4, 2005 (UUID namespacing).
  - **Details**: Build on the LIVE `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.ts` (RFC4122 run-id namespacing, `deriveRunNamespace`, `deriveClaimKey`, `countNamespaceCollisions` already shipped) and the LIVE `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (which already supports `--spawn-additional-workers=N`, worker-daemon liveness probe, and worker pause/resume). (a) Add a pre-spawn task-claim gate in `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` that calls `scripts/pick_task.py` per worker and refuses to assign an already-claimed task via `deriveClaimKey`-keyed O_EXCL lock files under the run namespace. (b) Wire `bin/minsky-run.sh` to accept `--workers-total N` and pass a per-worker run-id so each walk uses a disjoint namespace. (c) Extend `scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs` to assert zero collisions across the N-worker fanout. (d) Sweeper: prune stale worktrees/locks older than the iteration TTL every conductor tick.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.ts` (extend with stale-claim eviction), `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.test.ts`, `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (pre-spawn claim gate), `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs`, `bin/minsky-run.sh` (`--workers-total` flag), `scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs` + `.test.mjs`, `scripts/pick_task.py` (claim-aware skip)
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.test.ts`, `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs`, `bin/minsky-run.sh`, `scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs`, `scripts/pick_task.py`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `bin/minsky-run.sh --workers-total 3` spawns 3 disjoint-namespace walks with no path/lock/branch collision; (2) pre-spawn claim gate refuses an already-claimed task; (3) `scripts/chaos-multitenant.mjs` asserts 0 collisions across ≥100 runs; (4) stale-claim eviction runs each tick with paired tests; (5) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0) — provides the worker-spawn + claim substrate.
- [ ] `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` — Claude/cloud orchestrator (brain) fans work to N local/cheap workers in isolated run namespaces; chaos-engineered cross-layer stability
  - **ID**: claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED; block retained — test files freeform-cite this id; remove citation then block.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, orchestrator, parallel, worktree, chaos-engineering, role-separation
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: brain-vs-hands separation — a high-quality cloud model reviews/merges while cheap workers implement — is the throughput-per-dollar lever Minsky competes on vs single-model loops.
  - **Hypothesis**: Today `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` is the conductor (self-heal worker daemon + gate-then-review merge authority) and `bin/minsky-run.sh` resolves `cloud_agent`/`local_agent` from `~/.minsky/config.json`, but the role is not pinned per-process — a worker can still burn the cloud budget. Pinning orchestrator iterations to the cloud model and worker iterations to the configured local agent makes the cloud-budget belong to the brain; measured by ≥90% of cloud tokens spent by the orchestrator over a 24h window with N workers alive.
  - **Success**: over a steady 24h window with N=3 workers, orchestrator cloud-token share ≥0.9 AND `scripts/orchestrate.mjs --once` correctly skips non-gate-green PRs (no false merge) AND 0 zombie workers after an orchestrator kill.
  - **Pivot**: if orchestrator cloud-token share <0.7 (role-pin leaking), replace the soft preference with a hard env gate (`MINSKY_ROLE=worker` refuses cloud dispatch); if that still leaks, retire role-pin and run all workers on the local agent only.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/orchestrate.mjs --once --json | node -e 'let s="";process.stdin.on("data",d=>s+=d).on("end",()=>{const j=JSON.parse(s);process.exit((typeof j.merged!=="undefined"&&typeof j.skipped!=="undefined")?0:1)})'`
  - **Anchor**: Basiri et al., "Principles of Chaos Engineering", IEEE Software 2016 (steady-state hypothesis + fault injection); Hewitt, "A Universal Modular Actor Formalism", IJCAI 1973 (orchestrator + workers as message-passing actors).
  - **Details**: Compose the LIVE substrates: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (conductor: worker-daemon liveness, `--spawn-additional-workers=N`, pause/resume, gate-then-review merge), `bin/minsky-run.sh` (config-driven `cloud_agent`/`local_agent` resolution), `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-config.ts` (run namespacing from `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch`). (a) Add a role attribute to each worker spawn so the orchestrator's own iterations use `cloud_agent_model` while worker walks use `local_agent`/`local_agent_model`. (b) Add cross-layer chaos invariants to `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`: `orchestrator-budget-monopoly` (cloud-token ratio orchestrator:worker ≥9.0 when workers alive) and `orchestrator-detached-worker-finish` (workers finish or self-terminate cleanly when the orchestrator PID exits). (c) Chaos test `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` (paired with existing `chaos-multitenant.mjs`). (d) `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md` documents the role-separation rationale + failure-mode inventory.
  - **Files**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (role-pinned spawn + invariant wiring), `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs`, `bin/minsky-run.sh` (role-aware agent selection), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (two new invariants), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`, `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` + `.test.mjs`, `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md`
  - **Touches**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs`, `bin/minsky-run.sh`, `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`, `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs`
  - **Acceptance**: (1) orchestrator iterations use `cloud_agent_model`, worker walks use `local_agent` per role; (2) two new self-diagnose invariants ship with paired tests; (3) `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` proves workers finish or self-terminate (no zombie) with paired tests; (4) `scripts/orchestrate.mjs --once` skips non-gate-green PRs; (5) `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md` documents the role split + ≥4 cross-layer failure modes; (6) `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=fast` exits 0.
  - **Composes-with**: `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` (P0 — worker-spawn + claim substrate).

- [ ] `orchestrator-gh-graphql-401-token-source-divergence` — orchestrator sweep 401s on GitHub GraphQL every tick because the launchd process resolves a different (server-rejected) gh credential than an interactive shell
  - **ID**: orchestrator-gh-graphql-401-token-source-divergence
  - **Tags**: p1, reliability, orchestrator, auth, gate, rule-6, needs-user-approval
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Blocked**: needs-user-action — root remediation is rotating/refreshing the GitHub token and/or pinning the orchestrator to a known-good credential source; token rotation is a credential operation the operator must perform (interactive `gh auth login` or token reissue). Agent must not rotate credentials or propagate a leaked token into a plist. Unblock = operator confirms a valid GraphQL-scoped token is the one the launchd orchestrator resolves.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-17 live Opus-on-Opus supervision — `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` ticks at 05:13:14Z and 05:34:20Z both carry `sweepError:"Command failed: gh pr list --state open --limit 50 --json number,isDraft,mergeable,baseRefName,headRefName,title … HTTP 401: Requires authentication (https://api.github.com/graphql)"`. The SAME command + `gh api graphql {viewer{login}}` from an interactive shell succeed every time (≥3 consecutive). `com.minsky.orchestrator.plist` exports NO `GITHUB_TOKEN`; `gh auth status` lists two accounts — env `GITHUB_TOKEN` (Active=true) and `keyring` (Active=false), both `gho_` with identical scopes. The launchd orchestrator (no `GITHUB_TOKEN` in its environment) resolves the keyring credential, which is server-side-rejected for GraphQL, while the interactive shell uses the valid env token. (Note: during this diagnosis a token value was inadvertently echoed to the operator session — operator advised to rotate; that rotation also resolves this task.)
  - **Details**: `gh pr list --json mergeable,...` requires the GraphQL endpoint; REST-only calls may still pass, which is why the orchestrator process stays up (graceful-degrade, rule #7: logs `sweepError`, no crash, no spurious heal) but **never advances a merge** once the keyring token is GraphQL-invalid — silently degrading requirement-6 (autonomous merging) for all *future* PRs while already-merged ones (#591/#594/#580) stand. Fix has two independent parts: (a) **code/config** — make `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`'s gh invocations deterministically use a known-good credential (e.g., orchestrator reads a dedicated least-privilege token from a file referenced by the plist, or the plist pins `GH_TOKEN`/`GITHUB_TOKEN` via a non-secret indirection; document the resolution order so launchd ≡ interactive); (b) **detection** — classify a GraphQL-401 `sweepError` distinctly from a transient blip: N consecutive GraphQL-401 sweeps emit a loud `orchestrator.gh-auth-divergence` span / heartbeat field so it is not mistaken for the benign momentary 401s. Compose with the existing worker-side P1 [[tick-loop-transient-gh-401-must-not-crash-daemon]] (same symptom class, different component + root cause: that one = worker daemon crashing on transient 401; this one = orchestrator sweep persistently failing GraphQL due to which token the launchd env resolves).
  - **Files**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (gh invocation + credential resolution + sweepError classification), `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.minsky.orchestrator.plist` (credential indirection — operator-owned), heartbeat/monitor span for the divergence signal, paired test with an injected gh-exec seam
  - **Touches**: scripts/orchestrate.mjs, scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs
  - **Acceptance**: with a valid operator-provided credential source, the launchd orchestrator's `gh pr list --json mergeable` succeeds on the same ticks an interactive shell does (0 GraphQL-401 sweepErrors over 5 consecutive ticks); a deliberately-invalid credential produces a distinct `orchestrator.gh-auth-divergence` signal (not a silent benign-looking sweepError) within ≤2 ticks; orchestrator never `process.exit`s on the 401 (rule #6 preserved).
  - **Hypothesis**: pinning the orchestrator to a known-good credential source restores autonomous-merge-rate (DORA deployment-frequency) on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard from the current silently-degraded 0-merges-per-tick (post keyring-token rejection) back to the gate-green baseline; the distinct divergence signal cuts MTTR for this failure class from "invisible until a human reads orchestrate.jsonl" to ≤2 ticks.
  - **Success**: post-fix, ≥1 clean mergeable PR is autonomously merged within 3 ticks of becoming gate-green (was: 0, blocked by GraphQL-401); divergence span fires within 2 ticks on injected bad credential.
  - **Pivot**: if deterministic launchd credential resolution proves infeasible without storing a secret in the plist, fall back to a file-mode short-lived token the orchestrator reads at tick start (path in plist, secret out of plist) — and if even that is rejected, gate the merge step behind a REST-only mergeability heuristic (drop the GraphQL `mergeable` field; derive from `gh pr view --json state,mergeStateStatus` or a local `git merge-tree` dry-run) so autonomous merge survives GraphQL-auth loss.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c 'api.github.com/graphql' .minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` over a fixed window before/after → trends to 0 for the fixed credential; autonomous merges resume in `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` `merged:[…]`; injected-bad-credential test asserts the divergence span within 2 ticks.
  - **Anchor**: live Opus-on-Opus run 2026-05-17 (orchestrate.jsonl 05:13:14Z & 05:34:20Z GraphQL-401 sweepErrors; interactive gh + `gh api graphql` succeed; plist has no GITHUB_TOKEN; `gh auth status` env-vs-keyring divergence); GitHub docs (GraphQL requires auth; REST/GraphQL separate surfaces); vision.md rule #6 (let-it-crash at the right boundary — here the right boundary is "surface the auth divergence loudly", not "silently skip every merge forever"); rule #7 (graceful-degrade — already correct for *transient*, insufficient for *persistent*); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD).

Ping: maintainer `@Yeachan-Heo` (no other co-maintainers visible). Draft below — paste title in title field, paste body (between the fences, not including them) in the body field.

    ````markdown
    Title: Proposal: optional TASKS.md adapter for /team mode (ecosystem alignment with tasks.md spec)

    ## Summary

    Hi @Yeachan-Heo — proposing an optional adapter so `/team` mode can read its task list from a `TASKS.md` at repo root following the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md), with full backward compatibility (current behaviour is the default).

    The tasks.md spec is a minimal, plain-Markdown task-board format maintained by [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (kanban-style board renderer + linter). Multiple tools are converging on it as a portable task substrate: the upstream `tasksmd` toolchain itself, the Minsky project (constitutional rule: TASKS.md is the actor message store — Hewitt 1973), and any tool that wants its task list to be human-editable and version-controlled in the same file plain-text editors and `gh` already understand.

    OMC's `/team` mode already has a well-shaped persisted task store — this proposal is just to let users point that store at a Markdown file when they want a portable substrate.

    ## Where the integration would land (code-level)

    From a read of `Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode@main`:

    - `src/team/state-paths.ts` — `TeamPaths` declares the canonical layout (`.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`, `config.json`, `events.jsonl`, etc.). An adapter would add an alternate source resolver: when `config.json` carries `tasks_source: "tasks.md"`, the adapter reads `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` instead of the per-task JSON files. Default unchanged.
    - `src/team/types.ts` (lines ~38-58, ~195-213) — `TaskFile` / `TeamTask` shape: `id`, `subject`, `description`, `status`, `owner?`, `blocks[]`, `blocked_by?`, `created_at`, `version?`, `claim?`, etc. Maps cleanly to tasks.md fields:
      - `id` ↔ tasks.md `**ID**`
      - `subject` ↔ task title (the `- [ ]` / `- [x]` line)
      - `description` ↔ tasks.md `**Details**`
      - `status` (`pending | in_progress | completed | blocked`) ↔ `[ ]` / `[x]` checkbox + an extension `**Status**` field for the non-binary states
      - `owner` / `claim.owner` ↔ tasks.md `**Owner**`
      - `blocked_by` / `depends_on` ↔ tasks.md `**Blocked by**`
      - `created_at` ↔ provenance comment
      - `version` (optimistic concurrency) ↔ idempotency key in a hidden HTML comment, preserved on round-trip
    - `src/team/state/tasks.ts:90` — `writeAtomic(taskFilePath, JSON.stringify(updated, null, 2))` is the single canonical write site for `claimTask`. An adapter parallel to this would re-render the relevant tasks.md block (write-back is the harder direction; could ship in a v2).
    - `src/team/task-file-ops.ts:157, 210-243, 321-376` — read/write call sites; the read side is where the adapter reads tasks.md when `tasks_source: "tasks.md"` is set.

    The richer OMC v2 fields (`TeamTaskV2`'s `delegation_compliance`, `claim.token`, `claim.leased_until`) don't have natural tasks.md equivalents; the adapter would lossy-project them on read and preserve them in a hidden comment block on write so round-trips are non-destructive.

    ## Why this is ecosystem alignment, not a single-project request

    Three independent adopters of the tasks.md spec today:

    1. The spec maintainers themselves at [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (board renderer + linter — `npx @tasks-md/lint`).
    2. Minsky (long-running orchestration substrate; uses TASKS.md as its actor message store).
    3. Any tool that wants tasks to be `git`-diffable, plain-Markdown, editable in a plain-text editor without a runtime — a non-trivial superset given how many devs already keep a `TASKS.md` or `TODO.md` by convention.

    For OMC users specifically, this would mean: a team member without OMC installed can still read and edit the task list as plain Markdown; `gh` PR diffs show task changes in a human-readable format; the task list survives independently of `.omc/state/`.

    ## Concrete proposal

    Add an optional `tasks_source` field to `config.json`:

    ```json
    {
      "name": "my-team",
      "tasks_source": "tasks.md"
    }
    ```

    - When unset (default): current behaviour — read/write `.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`.
    - When `"tasks.md"`: read `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` per the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md); fall back to current behaviour if absent or malformed (with a warning).
    - v0 scope: read-only OMC ← TASKS.md (so OMC's optimistic-concurrency `version` field stays authoritative). Write-back can land in a v1 once the round-trip semantics are settled.

    No breaking changes to existing teams; no new required dependencies (a small Markdown parser would suffice, or `@tasks-md/lint`'s parser if you want to share the spec's reference implementation).

    ## Open question

    Does this fit `/team` mode's design intent — i.e., is the canonical task store something `/team` would want to be pluggable — or would you prefer this live as a separate plugin / adapter package (e.g., `@oh-my-claudecode/tasks-md-adapter`) so the core stays minimal? Happy to draft the PR either way; just want to follow your design preference before writing code.

    Thanks for OMC — `/team` mode's blackboard model is exactly the substrate this is trying to align with.
    ````

  - **Hypothesis**: Switching the auto-generated plist to `--hosts-dir <parent>` when ≥2 bootstrapped hosts exist (today: minsky + agentbrew) makes the daemon visit every bootstrapped host without manual editing.   - **Pivot**: if `--hosts-dir` triggers latent walker bugs that don't fire in single-host mode (e.g. `walker-task-rotation` blocking the whole walk on one starvation case), gate the multi-host emit behind `MINSKY_MULTI_HOST=1` for one release while those bugs land, but keep the doctor check on regardless so the operator sees the gap.

  - **Anchor**: cwd-detect.ts already provides the multi-host primitive (rule #1 — don't reinvent); host-walker.ts maps drain-then-advance over the host list (Liu & Layland 1973 — round-robin scheduling); 2026-05-20 audit log + the `walker-task-rotation` already-filed P0 (composing dependency — both fixes together unblock multi-host).
  - **Why P1 not P0**: not a correctness bug in the engine — the walker works correctly when invoked with `--hosts-dir`. The plist is just emitting the wrong flag. <!-- Observations filed 2026-05-18 from live daemon session (P1 findings). -->

- [ ] `metrics-render-finite-number-validation-bug` — `pnpm metrics:render` fails with `metric "loop-uptime" value must be a finite number` against today's snapshot at `.minsky/metric-snapshots/<date>.json`, blocking the daily refresh of `METRICS.md`; this caused the 2026-05-21 `check-metric-freshness` failure that took main red for ~24h and stalled the auto-merge gate (every PR's vet failed `vitest` on `metric-freshness` until the operator manually bumped the stale `_Updated` timestamps)
  - **ID**: metrics-render-finite-number-validation-bug
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Fix already landed on main (validator accepts strings, tests present, gate green); only TASKS.md closure remains.
  - **Tags**: p1, milestone-m1, observability, daemon, bug, observed-2026-05-21, rule-17, blocker
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-21 PR-drain session — discovered when the parallel auto-merge drain showed every PR failing on `gate red: vitest,metric-freshness`. Root cause: the daily metrics-render daemon step (`maybeRunMetricsRender` in `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`) silently failed to update `METRICS.md` because `scripts/metrics-render.mjs` errors on the snapshot `loop-uptime` field (`metric-snapshot-store.mjs:114 validateMetricEntry → must be a finite number`). The snapshot generator (`scripts/collect-metrics.mjs`) emits values for `loop-uptime` that aren't finite numbers (likely a percent-as-string like `"53.3%"` instead of a numeric `0.533`).
  - **Hypothesis**: `scripts/collect-metrics.mjs` writes the `loop-uptime` value as a string (`"53.3%"`) but `scripts/metric-snapshot-store.mjs:114 validateMetricEntry` requires a finite number. Fixing the collector to emit numeric values (with `_unit: "percent"` or `_unit: "fraction"` as a sibling key) plus relaxing the validator to accept the matching shape closes the loop. Same fix shape for any future percent/ratio metrics.
  - **Success**: (1) `pnpm metrics:render` exits 0 against today's snapshot. (2) The daily `maybeRunMetricsRender` step in `runDaemon` produces a fresh `METRICS.md` within the 1d freshness budget for `dep-interface-coverage` and `token-budget-honoring` (the 1d-budget metrics that went stale 2026-05-20 → 2026-05-21). (3) The `check-metric-freshness` lint stays green for ≥7 consecutive days without operator intervention.
  - **Pivot**: if `metrics-render` proves architecturally entangled with the snapshot format (e.g., a wider serialization-mismatch class than just `loop-uptime`), pivot to a snapshot-validation pre-step that converts string-percents → numeric-fractions at write time. Threshold: if fixing `loop-uptime` reveals ≥3 other metrics with similar type mismatches, the validator should be relaxed (with explicit `_unit` annotation) rather than each collector path patched individually.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm metrics:render && node scripts/check-metric-freshness.mjs` — both exit 0.
  - **Anchor**: rule #11 (vision.md § 11 — no flaky metric is load-bearing; metrics MUST be deterministic and freshly observed) composed with rule #17 (proactive healing — observation IS the fix; this bug surfaced during PR-drain ops and is being filed in the same session it was observed). Conformance pattern: validated-snapshot (Beyer SRE 2016 — schema-checked observation records).
  - **Details**: (a) Reproduce: `node scripts/collect-metrics.mjs && cat .minsky/metric-snapshots/$(date -u +%Y-%m-%d).json | jq '.metrics["loop-uptime"]'` shows the offending value shape. (b) Fix `scripts/collect-metrics.mjs` `loop-uptime` collector to emit `{ value: 0.533, _unit: "fraction" }` or similar numeric shape. (c) Verify `scripts/metric-snapshot-store.mjs` `validateMetricEntry` accepts the new shape; extend the validator if needed. (d) Re-run `pnpm metrics:render` against the fixed snapshot; verify `METRICS.md` regenerates with fresh `_Updated` timestamps. (e) Add a paired test asserting that `loop-uptime` collector output passes `validateMetricEntry`.
  - **Files**: `scripts/collect-metrics.mjs` (fix the collector); `scripts/metric-snapshot-store.mjs` (relax/extend validator if needed); paired test additions.
  - **Touches**: scripts/collect-metrics.mjs, scripts/metric-snapshot-store.mjs, .minsky/metric-snapshots/* (regenerated)
  - **Acceptance**: Measurement command exits 0. The daemon's `maybeRunMetricsRender` step completes successfully on its next daily firing (verified by checking `~/.minsky/daemon.log` for `metrics-render: ok`).
  - **Risk**: low. Pure type-fix in a well-isolated collector. The freshness lint is already passing against the bumped timestamps, so this fix is for the durable substrate (so the operator doesn't need to bump timestamps manually next week).
  - **Note**: composes with `canonical-metric-list-per-repo` (the broader metric-source curation task).

  - **ID**: investigate-claude-native-task-standard
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Deliverable doc already merged on main (PR #757); only TASKS.md block removal remains — orchestrator-owned.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, research, agent-teams, tasks-md, rule-1, rule-9, rule-14, replace-or-relocate
  - **Milestone**: M2
  - **Touches**: `docs/research/claude-native-task-standard.md`, `TASKS.md`, `vision.md`
  - **Competitive-goal**: if Claude's native task standard can replace minsky's hand-rolled TASKS.md tracking/claiming/lint stack, minsky deletes a whole owned subsystem (rule #14 scope-shrink) — lowering maintenance surface and raising native interop, which improves the cost-per-merged-PR and coordination-overhead lines on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard; the answer also de-risks (or redirects) the [[native-agent-teams-with-tiered-adapter]] bridge slice.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator directive 2026-05-17 ("claude has a standard for tasks — investigate it") + the agent-teams doc 2026-05-17 (native task list stored at `~/.claude/tasks/{team-name}/`, states pending/in-progress/completed, inter-task dependencies, file-locked claiming; the interactive-mode task list `/en/interactive-mode#task-list`; hooks `TaskCreated`/`TaskCompleted`). This is the first concrete instance of the new vision.md **rule #14** (delegate to agents; adopt native capabilities; shrink to fit).
  - **Details**: this is an investigation/spike — the deliverable is `docs/research/claude-native-task-standard.md`, not a code change (no production wiring in this task; it scopes the follow-ups). It must answer, with citations to the live Claude Code docs (start from the docs index `https://code.claude.com/docs/llms.txt`, then agent-teams + interactive-mode + hooks + settings pages): (a) **Is there a documented, stable task schema/standard?** exact on-disk format/location (`~/.claude/tasks/{team}/…`), fields, state machine, dependency model, claim/lock semantics, and whether it is a *supported public contract* vs an *experimental internal* layout (agent-teams is flagged experimental — weight this heavily). (b) **Gap vs minsky's TASKS.md** (the `tasks.md` spec: `## P0..P3`, checkbox tasks, bold metadata, `(@agent)` claim, kebab IDs, `npx @tasks-md/lint`): a field-by-field comparison matrix — what maps 1:1, what minsky has that the native standard lacks (priority sections, HDD fields, `**Competitive-goal**`, scout discipline), what the native standard has that minsky lacks (file-locked claim, native hook lifecycle, dependency auto-unblock). (c) **Three options costed**: (i) **Adopt** — minsky emits/consumes the native standard as source of truth, TASKS.md becomes a generated view; estimate the minsky modules/lines deletable. (ii) **Bridge** — keep TASKS.md authoritative, sync to the native list (this is the existing [[native-agent-teams-with-tiered-adapter]] slice (c)); estimate net scope delta (likely +). (iii) **Reject/Watch** — native standard too unstable/experimental to depend on; re-file as a monthly watch task per rule #14. (d) **Recommendation** with a single go/no-go and a quantified owned-surface delta (modules/lines added or removed), plus the migration risk to TASKS.md's scout/priority/HDD discipline (must not be lost — see CLAUDE.md tasks.md policy). (e) Coordinate with the `tasks.md` spec owners (tasksmd/tasks.md) if convergence is viable — note as a relocate candidate per rule #1.
  - **Files**: `docs/research/claude-native-task-standard.md` (new — the decision doc + comparison matrix + costed options + recommendation), `TASKS.md` (this block; on accept/bridge the doc files the concrete follow-up P0s), optionally `vision.md` Pattern-conformance-index row if a decision lands.
  - **Hypothesis**: today minsky owns a full bespoke task-tracking/claiming/lint stack while the agent runtime ships an overlapping native task standard; a rigorous comparison will show either (i) the native standard is a stable public contract → adopting it deletes ≥1 minsky subsystem with behavioural parity (rule #14 win), or (ii) it is experimental/internal → the correct answer is bridge-only + a monthly watch task. Pre-registration: the recommendation and the quantified scope-delta are written in the doc *before* any adoption code is filed.
  - **Success**: `docs/research/claude-native-task-standard.md` exists and contains (1) the exact native format/lifecycle/lock/dep semantics with doc citations; (2) the field-by-field comparison matrix vs the `tasks.md` spec; (3) the three options each with a quantified owned-surface delta (modules/lines); (4) a single explicit go/no-go recommendation; (5) the named follow-up tasks (P0 if scope-deleting) it would spawn; reviewed against rule #14's "must net-reduce owned surface" test.
  - **Pivot**: if no stable, documented public task standard exists (only the experimental agent-teams internal layout), do NOT design an adoption — the recommendation is "bridge-only, treat native task list as opaque, re-file `watch-claude-task-standard` as a monthly rule-#14 scan task"; never make the daemon depend on an experimental internal file layout (rule #6).
  - **Measurement**: deliverable-gated research task — `test -f docs/research/claude-native-task-standard.md` and a checklist assertion (a `scripts/check-research-doc.mjs`-style or manual reviewer rubric) that all five Success items are present incl. a numeric owned-surface delta; the follow-on adoption/bridge tasks (if any) carry their own HDD with the real before/after metric.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-17 (verbatim); vision.md **rule #14** (delegate/adopt-native/shrink — this task is its first scheduled instance), rule #1 (replace-or-relocate — `tasks.md` repo is the relocate candidate), rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — recommendation committed before adoption code), rule #12 (scope discipline — the costed options are scored on owned-surface delta); Claude Code docs 2026-05-17 (agent-teams task list `~/.claude/tasks/{team}/`, interactive-mode task list, `TaskCreated`/`TaskCompleted` hooks); the `tasks.md` spec (github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) as the incumbent standard. Composes [[native-agent-teams-with-tiered-adapter]] (its bridge slice is option (ii) here) and [[self-metrics-competitive-benchmark]] (scope-delta feeds the scorecard).

The `~/.agents/agents/security-reviewer.md` (and `~/.claude/agents/security-reviewer.md`) reference `skills: [code-secure-skill]`; OpenHands SDK's `register_file_agents` crashes with `ValueError: Skill 'code-secure-skill' not found` whenever Conversation.run() is called. Today this is worked around by a manual stub at `~/.openhands/skills/code-secure-skill/SKILL.md`; agentbrew should sync the canonical file directly
  - **ID**: agentbrew-sync-missing-private-skill-to-openhands
  - **Blocked**: needs-external-action — fix lives in the agentbrew repo (sync rule + marketplace-plugin handling), not in minsky. Filed here because minsky's smoke test discovered it; the unblock path is a PR in the agentbrew repo. Block lifts when the agentbrew side ships.
  - **Tags**: p2, scout-finding, agentbrew, openhands-sync, external-dep-needed, observed-2026-05-24
  - **Milestone**: M2
  - **Competitive-goal**: closes the "OpenHands SDK crashes when ANY agent references a private skill" failure mode. Without this, every operator who has the `security-reviewer` agent and tries to spawn OpenHands gets a hard crash before the agent can run.
  - **Hypothesis**: agentbrew's `~/.claude/skills/ → ~/.openhands/skills/` sync rule excludes skills from marketplace plugins (the ones under `~/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/`). The fix is to add marketplace-plugin skills to the sync set so every `skills:` reference in any agent definition resolves correctly. Falsifiable: if agentbrew already syncs marketplace skills and the private skill was sync'd correctly but then removed for some other reason, the fix is different.
  - **Success**: `find ~/.openhands/skills/code-secure-skill -name SKILL.md` returns a non-stub file; the OpenHands SDK conversation construction succeeds without a `Skill 'code-secure-skill' not found` error; the existing stub at `~/.openhands/skills/code-secure-skill/SKILL.md` (manually created 2026-05-24) is replaced by the canonical synced file.
  - **Pivot**: if agentbrew can't sync marketplace skills (e.g. policy reasons), the alternative is to add a `~/.openhands/agents/` sync rule that filters out agents whose `skills:` references can't be resolved — but that requires agentbrew to validate skill availability, which is heavier than just syncing the missing skill.
  - **Measurement**: `node -e "console.log(fs.existsSync(require('os').homedir() + '/.openhands/skills/code-secure-skill/SKILL.md'))"` returns true AND the file is NOT the placeholder stub (check for the "Placeholder stub" header text); `python3 -c "from openhands.sdk import LLM, Agent, Conversation, Tool; from openhands.tools.terminal import TerminalTool; conv = Conversation(agent=Agent(llm=LLM(model='ollama_chat/qwen3:0.6b', base_url='http://localhost:11434', api_key='x'), tools=[Tool(name=TerminalTool.name)]), workspace='/tmp')"` exits 0.
  - **Anchor**: scout finding from PR #786 (`feat/openhands-ollama-local-llm-support`); rule #17 (proactive healing — observation IS the fix); the agentbrew skill-sync invariant should be "every `skills:` reference in any agent definition under `~/.agents/` or `~/.claude/agents/` resolves to a real SKILL.md in `~/.openhands/skills/`" — that's a 1-line shell invariant the agentbrew test suite should enforce.
  - **Files**: agentbrew sync configuration (in the agentbrew repo, not this one); `~/.openhands/skills/code-secure-skill/SKILL.md` (currently a stub — to be replaced or removed); no minsky-repo files (this task is filed here because minsky's smoke test discovered it, but the fix lives upstream in agentbrew).
  - **Touches**: <none>

  - **ID**: vision-md-line-width-chunking
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — Long lines are pattern-index table rows; can't break cells without violating no-semantic-change criterion.

  - **Hypothesis**: replacing the 89 ultra-wide single-paragraph constitutional clauses with paragraph-broken equivalents reduces total file size and lets agents load `vision.md` into a smaller context-window budget while preserving 100% of the content. Falsifiable: a diff that adds only paragraph breaks (no semantic edits) should round-trip through a markdown parser with identical AST nodes except for paragraph splits.
  - **Success**: `awk '{ if(length > 1000) c++ } END { print c+0 }' vision.md` returns `0`; total byte size drops to ≤ 500 KB (currently 1.2 MB); a markdown parse comparison confirms semantic equivalence.

Per the load-project-context rule shipped via agentbrew, agents should treat it as system-prompt-level context. However, 89 of those lines are single ultra-wide paragraphs (max 14107 chars on one line). Most modern markdown editors and agents wrap on prose; the absence of paragraph breaks is likely an artifact of editor settings rather than a deliberate constitutional choice. Action: walk the file from top to bottom; for each line >1000 chars, identify natural sentence/clause boundaries (after `.`, `;`, or section markers like `—`) and insert paragraph breaks. Do not change wording, citations, rule numbers, or pattern conformance assertions. Run a diff afterward to confirm only whitespace and paragraph-break additions.

  - **Measurement**: A/B benchmark with the same HumanEval problem set: `bin/minsky benchmark humaneval --ensembling on` vs `bin/minsky benchmark humaneval --ensembling off`. JSON diff of `pass_at_1` and `total_cost_usd` must satisfy `pass_at_1_delta >= 0.05 AND cost_ratio <= 2.5`.

- [ ] `pre-pr-lint-biome-diff-scoped-vs-ci-whole-tree-divergence` — `pnpm pre-pr-lint` runs `biome ci --changed --since=origin/main` (diff-scoped), but the CI `biome` workflow job runs `biome ci .` (whole-tree). Formatting drift in unchanged files survives the local gate and explodes in CI 5 minutes later.
  - **ID**: pre-pr-lint-biome-diff-scoped-vs-ci-whole-tree-divergence
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p2, lint, biome, pre-pr-lint, ci-divergence, observed-2026-05-21
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-21 PM CI-stabilization sweep — PR #704 had to ship three pre-existing biome violations (in `scripts/heal-mttr-report.mjs`, `.releaserc.json`, `novel/tui/src/index.ts`) that the local diff-scoped gate didn't see because the files weren't in the PR's diff. Each CI failure required a separate fix PR (#705, #706, #707).
  - **Hypothesis**: the diff-scoped local gate is fundamentally a different gate from the whole-tree CI gate; a single PR's locally-green lint stack can't guarantee CI green. Two paths to reconcile: (a) make the local gate whole-tree too (slower but consistent) or (b) keep diff-scoped local but add an explicit `biome ci .` step to the lint stack's `full` stage so the whole-tree pass runs locally before push.
  - **Success**: after the fix, a PR that's clean against `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` never fails the CI `biome` job for unrelated whole-tree violations. Measurement: 5 consecutive PRs with this invariant.
  - **Pivot**: if making the local gate whole-tree exceeds 60s wall-clock on M2-class hardware (rule-#11 perf budget), keep diff-scoped local + add a separate `pnpm biome:full` script that runs in lefthook pre-push (not pre-commit).
  - **Measurement**: `time pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` p50/p95 over 10 runs after the fix; assert wall-clock budget ≤ 60s.
  - **Anchor**: rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — gates that disagree are non-deterministic); rule #11 (no flaky gates — a gate that says "ok" while the next gate says "fail" is flaky-by-construction); 2026-05-21 PR #704/#706/#707 chain.
  - **Files**: `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (the biome step args), `lefthook.yml` (pre-push hook reuse), `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (the biome job that exposes the whole-tree gap).
  - **Touches**: scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs, lefthook.yml, .github/workflows/ci.yml

- [ ] `pre-pr-lint-stack-vitest-hangs-vs-standalone` — `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` hangs in its `vitest` subprocess (10+ minutes, no output) while `npx vitest run` standalone completes in 33s with 3507/3518 passing
  - **ID**: pre-pr-lint-stack-vitest-hangs-vs-standalone
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p2, infra, pre-pr-lint, vitest, observed-2026-05-20
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-20 verify cycle for `agents-can-self-heal-minsky-m1-13` (PR opening from `plan/agents-self-heal-minsky`). Standalone `npx vitest run --testTimeout=15000 --bail=1 --reporter=verbose` completed in 33.56s with `3507 passed | 2 skipped | 9 todo (3518)`. The same vitest invoked by `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs`'s `vitest` step (via `pnpm test`) hung for >10 min in two separate runs; killing the process and re-running standalone reproduced the green result. All other 45 gates in the lint stack ran <2.5s.
  - **Details**: Diagnose why `pnpm test` invoked by the lint stack hangs but the same vitest invoked directly doesn't. Suspects: (a) the lint stack runs vitest under `tee` to a file, which may block stdin pipe / buffering; (b) `vitest.config.ts` has `retry: 2` which can multiply duration on a flaky test, possibly compounding under the stack's runner; (c) coverage instrumentation kicks in only via `pnpm test` (not `npx vitest run`) and hangs on a specific worker; (d) lefthook pre-pr-lint pre-push gates re-invoke vitest recursively. Find the root cause; fix it OR add a `--reporter=basic --bail=1` to the lint stack's vitest invocation so it surfaces hangs as test failures within 60s.
  - **Files**: `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (the lint stack runner), `vitest.config.ts` (retry config), `package.json` (`test` script), `lefthook.yml` (pre-push wiring).
  - **Touches**: scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs,vitest.config.ts,package.json,lefthook.yml
  - **Hypothesis**: a specific test or worker in the full vitest suite blocks indefinitely when stdout is piped through `tee`, but not when output goes directly to the terminal. Falsifiable: `pnpm test 2>&1 | tee /tmp/x.log` reproduces the hang while `pnpm test` (no pipe) completes; OR running `npx vitest run` with the exact `pnpm test` args reproduces the hang.
  - **Success**: `pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` completes (success or failure) within 5 minutes wall-clock on the M2-class fleet host. Falsifiable: run 10 times; ≥9 complete within 5 min OR a deterministic failure is reported.
  - **Pivot**: if the hang is in vitest itself (not the stack's runner), file upstream + work around by running `npx vitest run` instead of `pnpm test` in the stack.
  - **Measurement**: `time pnpm pre-pr-lint --stage=full` wall-clock; sample 10 runs; histogram p50/p95.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md row 73 (`scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` — the lint stack runner pattern); AGENTS.md rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — a gate that can't terminate isn't a gate); operator directive 2026-05-20 (verify M1.13 PR before push).

- [ ] `runany-permission-scoped-writes` — home repo: push commits + open PRs for any task; foreign repos under the tree: ONLY open a PR adding tasks to their TASKS.md from findings (never push code); always self-monitor minsky-on-itself and file improvement tasks into minsky's TASKS.md
  - **ID**: runany-permission-scoped-writes
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id. Convert citations to self-doc headers, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, runany, security, policy, rule-13
  - **Milestone**: M4
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/**`, `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs`
  - **Details**: a deterministic policy seam classifies each repo the run touches as **home** (the invoked folder's git repo / its origin) or **foreign** (any other git repo under the tree). Home → existing full flow (branch, push, PR, gate-merge). Foreign → the ONLY permitted write is `gh pr create` whose diff is limited to that repo's `TASKS.md` (append findings as tasks.md-spec task blocks); any non-TASKS.md change or push to a foreign repo is refused and logged. Independently, every run also vets minsky-on-itself and, on any friction/bug/regression, appends a task to minsky's own TASKS.md (scout-and-record across the fleet). Pure `classifyRepo()` + `assertWriteAllowed()` (rule #10, no model in the gate).
  - **Hypothesis**: without this, a run-anywhere conductor could push code to unrelated repos. After this, 0 code pushes to foreign repos occur; foreign-repo contributions are 100% TASKS.md-only PRs; minsky-self findings are filed every run that observes one.
  - **Success**: in a fixture with 1 home + 2 foreign repos, over a run: foreign repos receive only TASKS.md-only PRs (`gh pr diff` touches only TASKS.md), 0 foreign code pushes; ≥1 minsky-self improvement task filed when a seeded friction exists.
  - **Pivot**: if `gh pr diff`-shaped enforcement is bypassable, gate at the git layer (refuse `git push` whose remote ≠ home origin) as the hard backstop and keep the diff-shape check as defense-in-depth.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/runany-policy-audit.mjs --window=run --json` → `{foreign_code_pushes:0, foreign_prs_nontaskmd:0, minsky_self_tasks_filed:>=1}`.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security/privacy — least-authority across repos); Saltzer & Schroeder 1975 (least privilege, fail-safe defaults); operator 2026-05-16 directive.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/repo-policy.ts` (+ `.test.ts`), wiring in `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` + `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs`, `scripts/runany-policy-audit.mjs` (+ test), `docs/run-anywhere.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `classifyRepo`/`assertWriteAllowed` shipped with paired tests (home vs foreign × push/PR/taskmd cells); (2) foreign push of non-TASKS.md refused + logged; (3) minsky-self scout files a task on seeded friction; (4) measurement thresholds met.

- [ ] `runany-self-restart-bounded-timelimit` — on any crash/error the run auto-restarts with sensible escalating backoff, repeatedly, until a configured wall-clock time limit, then stops cleanly
  - **ID**: runany-self-restart-bounded-timelimit
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id. Convert citations to self-doc headers, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, runany, stay-alive, rule-6
  - **Milestone**: M4
  - **Touches**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs`, `bin/minsky`, `distribution/launchd/**`
  - **Details**: a supervising wrapper (launchd KeepAlive + an inner deadline guard) restarts the conductor on crash/non-zero exit with escalating backoff (e.g. 5s→15s→60s→300s, capped) that RESETS after a sustained-healthy interval; a `MINSKY_RUN_TIME_LIMIT` (default e.g. 10h) is the hard wall-clock ceiling after which the wrapper stops restarting and exits 0 cleanly. Composes launchd `ThrottleInterval` + `tick-loop-backoff-schedule`; new = the deadline guard + backoff-reset-on-health + clean terminal stop.
  - **Hypothesis**: today launchd restarts indefinitely with a flat throttle and no time ceiling. After this, an injected crash-loop backs off on the documented schedule, recovers (backoff resets) when healthy, and the process stops cleanly at the time limit (no zombie, no infinite restart past the deadline).
  - **Success**: chaos: kill the conductor every 30s for 10 min → restart intervals follow the escalating schedule, then a 20-min healthy window resets backoff to base; with `MINSKY_RUN_TIME_LIMIT=600s` the wrapper exits 0 within 600±30s and no restart fires after.
  - **Pivot**: if backoff-reset-on-health oscillates, use a fixed escalating schedule with no reset (simpler, still bounded) and document the throughput tradeoff.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/chaos-restart-schedule.mjs --json` → `{schedule_followed:true, reset_on_health:true, stopped_at_limit:true, restarts_after_limit:0}`.
  - **Anchor**: Armstrong 2007 (supervisor restart); Beyer SRE 2016 (retry budget / backoff); rule #6 (stay alive, but bounded); operator 2026-05-16 directive.
  - **Files**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (deadline + backoff), `bin/minsky` (wrapper), `distribution/launchd/com.minsky.runany.plist.tmpl`, `scripts/chaos-restart-schedule.mjs` (+ test), `docs/run-anywhere.md`.

- [ ] `secret-scanning-precommit-and-ci` — gitleaks (or trufflehog) scan in pre-commit + CI; secrets detected = block merge
  - **ID**: secret-scanning-precommit-and-ci
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — obsolete (test-cited; remove the test citation, then this block): Feature shipped via rule-#1 in-tree path: `scripts/scan-secrets.mjs` is wired into lefthook pre-commit AND the CI `secret-scan` job (in the aggregator `needs:` + result check). Blo
  - **Tags**: security, p0, leak-prevention, rule-10
  - **Milestone**: M4
  - **Touches**: `.lefthook.yml`, `lefthook.yml`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `.gitleaks.toml`, `docs/security/secret-scanning.md`
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: The supervisor edits arbitrary files in the repo per iteration (including config, env templates, plist files); without a deterministic gate, a single regression can write `OPENAI_API_KEY=...` / `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=...` / a private RSA key into a tracked file and push it. Industry baseline: Anthropic / GitHub / npm / etc. all rotate compromised tokens within 24h of detection, but the leak window before detection is real (median TTD for leaked tokens on public GitHub is hours; Truffle Security 2023 study). A `gitleaks` (or `trufflehog`) scan in lefthook pre-commit + GH Actions CI catches secrets before they ship. **Pre-registration**: 0 secrets in the repo at baseline (verified by initial scan); 0 secrets allowed to land in any future PR. Pivot if scan rate is too noisy (>2 false positives per month → tune the allow-list / gitleaks `.gitleaks.toml` config).
  - **Details**: (a) Add `gitleaks` to lefthook's pre-commit hook (already used for biome/typecheck/test); fail commit on any finding. (b) Add `.github/workflows/ci.yml` job `secret-scan` that runs `gitleaks detect --redact --no-banner --exit-code 1` on the PR diff; mark `needs:` in the `ci` aggregator. (c) `.gitleaks.toml` config tuned for the project — start with the default ruleset, allow-list any false positives encountered (each allow-list entry must reference a TASKS-id justifying the exclusion). (d) **One-time historical audit**: run `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all"` against all reachable history; any historical leak goes into a P0 rotation task (separate; needs immediate human approval per the no-cross-repo / no-message-board rule, since rotating an API key is a human-visible action). (e) Operator escape hatch: `MINSKY_SKIP_SECRET_SCAN=1` for the local pre-commit hook only (NOT for CI — CI is non-bypassable).
  - **Files**: `.lefthook.yml` (new pre-commit step), `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (new job + needs entry), `.gitleaks.toml` (new — tuned config), `docs/security/secret-scanning.md` (operator guide explaining the override + how to add allow-list entries).
  - **Verification**: paired tests via fixture commits (a synthetic test with a fake AWS-style key in a temp branch — `gitleaks` rejects it; same fixture without the key — passes); CI job blocks merge on the seeded fixture; `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all"` against current main returns 0 findings.
  - **Measurement**: `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all" --no-banner --exit-code 1; echo $?` returns 0 against main (no historical leaks). After merge: `gh api repos/fyodoriv/minsky/actions/workflows --jq '.workflows[] | select(.name == "secret-scan") | .state'` returns "active". Per-PR: every PR's checks include a passing `secret-scan` job.
  - **Pivot**: if gitleaks's default ruleset produces ≥3 false positives in the first month, swap to trufflehog (more aggressive entropy detection but more tunable per-pattern). The lefthook + CI integration is reversible — only the scanner binary changes.
  - **Acceptance**: zero secrets in current main (verified by full-history scan); pre-commit hook blocks new secrets locally; CI blocks new secrets on every PR; the historical-audit task is filed as a separate task (since rotation is a human action).
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #1, "no secrets in the repo, ever"); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — secret detection is a CI lint, not a hope); Truffle Security "The State of Secrets Sprawl 2023" (median TTD for public GitHub secrets is in hours; the cost of a leak is real); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 5 (defence in depth — pre-commit catches operator slips; CI catches everything else); rule #2 (the scanner is a Strategy seam — gitleaks → trufflehog pivot is one config change).
  - **Risk**: low-medium. False positives are the main operational risk; mitigation is the allow-list + pivot threshold.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything."

- [ ] `otel-no-pii-in-spans-lint` — CI lint that blocks any `record({...})` call carrying PII-shaped attributes
  - **ID**: otel-no-pii-in-spans-lint
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — obsolete (test-cited; remove the test citation, then this block): Fully shipped: scripts/check-otel-no-pii.mjs (classifier+AST walker+allow-annotation, exits 0), 59 paired tests pass, CI 'otel-no-pii' job wired into needs:+aggregate, docs/securit
  - **Tags**: security, p0, otel, observability, leak-prevention, rule-10
  - **Milestone**: M4
  - **Touches**: `scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii*.mjs`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml`
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Hypothesis**: Every `record({...})` call in `novel/**/*.ts` becomes an OTEL span. Spans flow to OpenObserve (and, in the cloud tier, to a multi-tenant aggregator). A regression that puts a Claude API key in a span (`record({apiKey: env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY})` is an easy mistake) leaks across the whole pipeline. The lint scans for: attribute names matching `(api[_-]?key|password|token|secret|credential|bearer)` or values matching `(sk-[a-zA-Z0-9]{20,}|ghp_[a-zA-Z0-9]{30,})` and rejects them. **Pre-registration**: 0 PII-shaped attributes across all current `record({...})` calls (verified via initial sweep); 0 allowed in any future PR. Pivot if the regex is too narrow (a leak-class slips through) or too noisy (≥2 false positives per month → refine rules).
  - **Details**: (a) `scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs` — regex over `record\(\{[^}]+\}\)` call sites in `novel/**/*.ts`. (b) Pure decision function `classifySpanAttribute(name, value): {ok: boolean, reason?: string}` with paired tests. (c) Allow-list: explicit annotations like `// @otel-pii-allowed: <reason>` next to a flagged line, recording why this particular attribute is intentionally PII-shaped (e.g., a hash of an opaque ID where the regex false-positives on the `_token` substring). Each allow-list usage requires a TASKS-id justifying it.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs` + paired tests, `.github/workflows/ci.yml` job + `needs:` entry.
  - **Verification**: ≥6 paired tests (token-named-attribute / sk-prefixed-value / password-named / safe-attribute-name / annotated-allowlist-honored / nested-object-traversed); CI job runs on every PR.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs --diff-base=origin/main` exits 0 against current main (no leaks today). Synthetic fixture: `test/fixtures/otel-pii/leaking-span.ts` containing `record({apiKey: env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY})` makes the lint exit 1.
  - **Pivot**: if the regex misses a leak class (e.g., the operator names a field `userPassphrase` instead of `password`), extend the regex with a learned pattern; the allow-list grows when refinement causes a false positive. Don't drop the lint — the alternative is "trust the operator", which is exactly what fails.
  - **Acceptance**: 0 PII-shaped attributes in current spans; lint blocks new ones; doc in `docs/security/otel-no-pii.md` explains what counts.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #2, "no PII in OTEL spans"); rule #4 (OTEL coverage; this is the security companion); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement); GDPR Art. 25 (data protection by design); CCPA equivalent in California; OWASP A04 "Insecure Design".
  - **Risk**: low. Static regex over source code; both false-positive and false-negative are tunable.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything."

- [ ] `cloud-tier-external-security-audit-gate` — block the cloud tier ship until a third-party security audit clears
  - **ID**: cloud-tier-external-security-audit-gate
  - **Tags**: security, p0, audit, cloud-tier, blocked-until-cloud-readiness
  - **Milestone**: M4
  - **Touches**: `scripts/check-cloud-audit-gate*.mjs`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `docs/security/audit-gate.md`
  - **Estimate**: external — 4-8w from when triggered
  - **Blocked**: needs-user-approval — engaging an external security audit firm is a human action (vendor selection, contract, payment) and out of scope for autonomous loops per `feedback_modify_only_minsky_repo.md`. Filed here so the gate exists in advance of the cloud tier shipping; user must approve in a separate session before this task starts.
  - **Hypothesis**: The local CLI's blast radius is the operator's own machine (already heavily mitigated by the other 5 P0 tasks here). The cloud tier's blast radius is **every customer's repo**, **every customer's API tokens**, and **every customer's data flowing through the multi-tenant OTEL aggregator**. Self-audit is insufficient — operators / customers correctly discount internal claims. **Pre-registration**: before any cloud tier feature ships to a non-operator user, an external firm (Trail of Bits / NCC Group / Doyensec / a comparable specialist) audits the threat model + sample implementation; their report is public (or at minimum the executive summary is); their critical findings are remediated and re-tested before the gate clears. Pivot if the audit cost exceeds the cloud tier's projected MRR for 12 months — postpone the cloud tier until the unit economics support a real audit; don't ship cloud-multi-tenant without one.
  - **Details**: (a) Block any PR that touches `novel/cloud-supervisor/`, `novel/cross-repo-benchmark/`, or `novel/shared-invariant-catalog/` (when those packages exist) until this task's `**Blocked**` line is removed. The block is enforced by a CI lint that scans for those package paths in the PR diff. (b) Scope of audit: cloud-supervisor's GH App auth flow, multi-tenant data isolation, OTEL ingestion pipeline, billing-once-paywall-lands. (c) Findings tracker: each finding is a P0 sub-task; gate clears only when all P0 sub-tasks ship.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-cloud-audit-gate.mjs` + tests, `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (new lint), `docs/security/audit-gate.md` (operator-facing — explains the gate + the unblock criteria).
  - **Verification**: synthetic PR touching `novel/cloud-supervisor/` is rejected by the lint; same diff after this task's `**Blocked**` line is removed → accepted.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-cloud-audit-gate.mjs --diff=test/fixtures/cloud-tier-without-audit.diff` exits 1; same with audit-cleared fixture exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if no external audit firm has bandwidth in a 4-8w window, the gate stays — the cloud tier just doesn't ship. Don't auto-clear the gate based on internal review alone (that's exactly the failure mode the audit prevents).
  - **Acceptance**: gate lint shipped + `needs:`-ed; cloud-tier sub-tasks (in the `paid-tier-features-skeleton` block) reference this gate as a prerequisite; doc explains what triggers the gate clear.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #6, "external security audit gate before cloud tier"); CNCF Security TAG's recommendation that multi-tenant infra ships with third-party audit; the empirical reality that every cloud-SaaS breach since 2020 (Log4Shell-adjacent, MOVEit, etc.) was eventually caught by external researchers — internal review is insufficient; rule #1 (use the existing audit-firm market — don't reinvent).
  - **Risk**: low for the gate itself (small CI lint); high for the cloud tier as a whole (this gate is what makes that risk manageable).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything." Pairs with `paid-tier-features-skeleton` (P3) — this gate is the security prerequisite for that task's cloud sub-tasks.

- [ ] `gate-host-load-shed` — shed concurrent host load during a merge-gate vet so vitest stops flaking under 2-3x oversubscription
  - **ID**: gate-host-load-shed
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: gate, reliability, performance, orchestrator
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: raises minsky's autonomous-merge-rate + lowers change-fail-rate (DORA) on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard by removing the last spurious-skip cause.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 root-caused the residual merge-rate-0 tail: with #590/#592/#593 + the 60-min vet timeout, the orchestrator's scratch vet of the clean MERGEABLE #591 still SKIP'd `gate red: vitest`. Isolated reproduction of the EXACT scratch (origin/main + #591 + `pnpm install` + `vitest`) passed **3039/3040** — the gate failure was a **load flake**: the host runs the orchestrator + worker daemon + other tenants concurrently at load ~14-26 on 10 cores, and a timing-sensitive test flaked under contention. Mitigated in the same PR by `vitest retry: 2` (a flake fails-then-passes; a real bug fails every attempt — Fowler 2011). This companion adds the durable structural fix: during a gate vet, shed competing load — e.g. pause/`SIGSTOP` the worker daemon's active iteration for the vet's duration, or `taskpolicy`/nice the scratch vet onto reserved cores, or serialize gate-vet vs worker-tick so they never run vitest simultaneously. Retry masks the symptom; this removes the cause.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (load-shed hook around `defaultVet`), `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (coordinate with worker daemon), paired tests
  - **Touches**: scripts/local-gate-merge*,scripts/orchestrate.mjs
  - **Acceptance**: during a gate vet, host load attributable to the worker daemon drops measurably (or vet runs on reserved cores); a 10-run gate-vet sample of a known-green PR yields 0 spurious `vitest` skips (was: intermittent under load).
  - **Hypothesis**: with load shedding, spurious `vitest` gate-red on green PRs → ~0; orchestrator autonomous-merge-rate per productive tick rises (retry alone leaves vet wall-time high under load).
  - **Success**: 10 consecutive gate vets of a seeded green PR all reach `gate green` (no vitest flake); vet p95 wall-time drops vs. the unshed baseline.
  - **Pivot**: if cooperative pause of the worker daemon is too invasive, fall back to retry-only (this PR) + raising `retry` to 3 and accept slower-but-correct vets.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c 'gate red: vitest' .minsky/orchestrate.out.log` over a fixed window before/after → trends to 0 for green PRs; vet p95 from `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` timing.
  - **Anchor**: Fowler 2011 *Eradicating Non-Determinism in Tests*; Nygard 2018 *Release It!* (resource contention / bulkhead); vision.md rule #6.

- [ ] `worker-liveness-detect-by-label-not-argv` — `workerDaemonAlive()` greps `tick-loop.mjs --worker-id=0`; with `--spawn-additional-workers=N` the root argv has no `--worker-id=0`, so liveness detection is fragile/coincidental
  - **ID**: worker-liveness-detect-by-label-not-argv
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id (check-task-block-citations gate). Operator: convert those citations to self-doc headers OR drop them, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: orchestrator, healing, detection, reliability, rule-6
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Competitive-goal**: a correct worker-liveness signal prevents spurious daemon kickstarts (avoids interrupting in-flight Opus iterations) → higher effective worker throughput on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 scaled workers to 4 via plist `--spawn-additional-workers=3` (root = worker-0, children `--worker-id=1/2/3`). `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` `workerDaemonAlive()` (line ~53) and the external heartbeat both do `pgrep -f 'tick-loop.mjs --worker-id=0'` — the root proc's argv is now `--spawn-additional-workers=3` (no `--worker-id=0` substring) and no child is `--worker-id=0`, so the intended match is gone. It currently returns true only because a STRAY pre-reload worker proc (old `--worker-id=0 --workers-total=1` argv) happens to still be running; if that stray exits, `workerDaemonAlive()` flips false and the conductor kickstarts the (healthy) 4-worker daemon every tick — disruptive churn that SIGKILLs in-flight Opus iterations. Heartbeat already false-alarms `worker=DOWN`. Fix: detect daemon liveness by launchctl label (`launchctl print gui/$uid/com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run` state=running, runs/last-exit) — the daemon's actual supervisor truth — instead of an argv-substring grep that breaks on any arg-shape change. Update the heartbeat probe identically.
  - **Files**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (`workerDaemonAlive` → launchctl-label probe), heartbeat/monitor script, paired test in a new `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs` (or extend) with injected probe
  - **Touches**: scripts/orchestrate.mjs,scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs
  - **Acceptance**: `workerDaemonAlive()` returns true whenever `com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run` is launchd-running regardless of `--worker-id`/`--spawn-additional-workers` arg shape, and false only when the agent is genuinely down; paired test covers both via injected launchctl-state seam; no kickstart when the daemon is up under `--spawn-additional-workers`.
  - **Hypothesis**: spurious worker-daemon kickstarts → 0 (currently latent: would fire every tick if the stray proc exits); in-flight Opus iterations no longer SIGKILLed by false heals.
  - **Success**: with the 4-worker daemon up, `decideHeal` returns "ok" across 5 consecutive ticks even after the stray `--worker-id=0` proc is killed; heartbeat reports worker=up.
  - **Pivot**: if launchctl-label parsing is brittle across macOS versions, fall back to a sentinel file the worker root touches each tick + an mtime-freshness check.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c 'healed.*true\|kickstarted com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run' .minsky/orchestrate.out.log` over a window with the daemon healthy → 0; ledger `healed:false` stays consistent after killing the stray proc.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (supervisor owns restart — detect via the supervisor, not a brittle process-argv heuristic); Nygard 2018 *Release It!* (health checks must reflect real liveness, not a proxy that drifts).

- [ ] `gate-vet-timeout-circuit-breaker` — a PR that vet-times-out should be skipped for a cooldown instead of re-consuming a bounded sweep slot every tick
  - **ID**: gate-vet-timeout-circuit-breaker
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — PR #1085 closed (branch kept): additive conflict with #1081 in local-gate-merge.mjs prepareSweep — needs careful operator union-rebase
  - **Tags**: gate, orchestrator, reliability, candidate-starvation
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Details**: Companion to the mergeability pre-resolution fix (this PR makes `defaultSnapshot` resolve TRUE mergeability via `gh pr view` so `pickGateCandidates` actually drops CONFLICTING PRs before the `limit` slice — previously `gh pr list` returned `UNKNOWN`, conflicts slipped to the 25-min scratch vet, and with `limit=2` the conductor perpetually re-vetted #577/#580 and never reached a mergeable PR: the merge-rate-0 starvation). Conflicts are now cheap-skipped, but a PR that genuinely vet-*times-out* (e.g. #580, a slow/hung test) still burns one full `MINSKY_GATE_VET_TIMEOUT_MS` (~25 min) slot on EVERY tick forever. Add a circuit-breaker: record per-PR-head timeout strikes (e.g. `.minsky/gate-timeout-strikes.json`, keyed by PR number + head SHA so a new push clears it) and skip a PR with ≥N recent strikes for a cooldown window, so one pathological PR cannot indefinitely consume the bounded sweep.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (strike record in `vetErrorToResult`/`processOnePr`, skip in `prepareSweep`), `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs` (paired: strike accrues on timeout; skipped within cooldown; cleared on new head SHA)
  - **Touches**: scripts/local-gate-merge*
  - **Acceptance**: a PR that timed out ≥2 ticks is pre-skipped (logged `timeout-circuit-open`) and consumes 0 vet slots until cooldown elapses OR its head SHA changes; non-timeout skips never accrue strikes; paired tests cover accrue/skip/clear.
  - **Hypothesis**: with conflicts cheap-skipped (this PR) AND timeouts circuit-broken (this task), a bounded `limit=2` sweep reaches a mergeable PR within 1 tick instead of never; orchestrator merge-rate per productive tick goes 0 → ≥1.
  - **Success**: in a sweep where candidates are [conflict, timeout-striked, green], only the green PR is vetted and it merges.
  - **Pivot**: if head-SHA-keyed strike state proves fragile across force-pushes, fall back to a simple per-PR-number N-strikes-then-cooldown with a short TTL.
  - **Measurement**: `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` — first `merged:[…]` non-empty tick after deploy; vet-slots-spent-on-timeouts per tick before/after.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (bounded, supervised) + rule #10; Nygard 2018 *Release It!* — Circuit Breaker stability pattern.
- [ ] `gate-scratch-resolvable-ratchet` — add a deterministic check that the local-merge-gate's scratch clone yields a module-resolvable workspace, so the zero-merge regression cannot recur silently
  - **ID**: gate-scratch-resolvable-ratchet
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — DELIVERED (merged); block retained — test files freeform-cite this id. Convert citations to self-doc headers, then delete this block.
  - **Tags**: gate, ratchet, rule-10, regression-guard
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Details**: On 2026-05-16 the Opus orchestrator merged 0 PRs across every tick. Root cause: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` `prepareScratchClone` symlinked only the *root* `node_modules`, but pnpm scatters a per-package `node_modules` symlink-farm across the workspace. A `git clone` scratch therefore had no nested `node_modules`, so `tsc -b` and `vitest` failed `Cannot find module` / `Failed to load url` for EVERY PR → the conductor correctly-but-uselessly skipped all of them. Fixed in the same PR by replacing the root-only symlink with an isolated `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile --prefer-offline --ignore-scripts` (warm store ⇒ ~3.6s). The bug was silent because an infra-broken vet was misattributed as a per-PR gate-red. This task adds the *rule* so the class cannot return: a check that fails CI if the gate's scratch-prep cannot resolve a known workspace import.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs`, `scripts/` (new `check-gate-scratch-resolvable` + paired test), `package.json` (wire into the verify gate)
  - **Acceptance**: a deterministic check (a) builds a throwaway scratch via the real `prepareScratchClone` path, (b) asserts resolution succeeds for a representative workspace pkg (`@minsky/adapter-types`) AND a registry dep (`@opentelemetry/api`), (c) fails loudly if either is unresolvable; wired into `npm run verify`; paired unit test proves it goes red when the install step is stubbed out.
  - **Hypothesis**: with the ratchet present, a future edit that reverts `prepareScratchClone` to symlink-only (or otherwise breaks scratch resolution) fails the verify gate before it can merge, so the recurrence mode changes from "silent until a human notices 0 merges" to "caught at PR time".
  - **Success**: stubbing the install step makes the check exit non-zero; the unmodified path exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if standing up a full scratch in the check is too slow for `verify` (>30s), assert the invariant structurally instead — grep that `prepareScratchClone` performs a real install and not a bare root-only symlink — accepting the weaker guarantee.
  - **Measurement**: `npm run verify` exit code with vs. without the install step stubbed; CI duration delta < 30s.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #10 (deterministic enforcement / ratchet); global rule "every bug becomes a rule — prevent the category, not the instance".
  - **ID**: dependabot-bumps-dep-regression-triage
  - **Tags**: p2, dependencies, ergonomics, dependabot
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: 9h window 2026-05-07: 8 dependabot PRs (`actions/setup-python` 5→6, `actions/upload-artifact` 4→7, `markdownlint-cli2` 0.15→0.22, `hono` 4.12.16→4.12.18, OTEL 0.57.2→0.217.0 ×3, etc.) all failing CI. Most are major bumps with breaking-change semantics; some are patch bumps that should pass. Pre-registration: post-fix, dependabot PRs split by semver: patch+minor auto-merge if CI green; major bumps file a `dep-upgrade-<package>` task with the breaking-change diff and require operator approval. Rolling-7d failing-dependabot-PR count → ≤2.
  - **Details**: `.github/dependabot.yml` configures `versioning-strategy: increase` for patch + minor; major bumps go to a separate group with `labels: [needs-operator]`. Existing 8 PRs: triage manually — close the major OTEL bumps as out-of-scope, retry the patch bumps after main updates.
  - **Files**: `.github/dependabot.yml`, `docs/dependency-policy.md`.
  - **Touches**: .github/dependabot.yml, docs/dependency-policy.md

  - **Measurement**: count of `closed-as-not-planned` dependabot PRs over 30d ≤ 1/month average.

  - **Anchor**: 9h window 2026-05-07; Dependabot best practices.
  - **Risk**: low.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window — 8 stuck dependabot PRs.

- [ ] `docs-operator-troubleshooting-prompt-too-long` — add a troubleshooting doc covering the `claude --print` prompt-too-long failure on heavy `~/.claude/` setups

  - **ID**: docs-operator-troubleshooting-prompt-too-long
  - **Blocked**: needs-operator — README byte-budget gate (3072B ceiling, 22B free) blocks required operator-troubleshooting link
  - **Tags**: documentation, operator-experience, claude-code, p2, surfaced-by-managed-host-b-monitoring
  - **Milestone**: M1
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: On machines with a heavy `~/.claude/` ecosystem (many skills + plugins + agents + rules accumulated over months — e.g. 92MB plugin marketplaces, 1GB session history, 74KB+ CLAUDE.md), `claude --print` exits 1 with "Prompt is too long" before processing any user input — the auto-loaded system prompt alone exceeds the model context. The documented escape hatches (`--bare`, `--setting-sources project,local`, `--disable-slash-commands`) have caveats: `--bare` disables OAuth/keychain auth (requires `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`), and `--setting-sources` doesn't prune plugin/skill auto-loading. Today's MINSKY workaround is `MINSKY_WORKER=devin` (PR #4bb10f9 on `feat/devin-as-headless-worker`). Adding `docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` with the symptom → root cause → workarounds → verification path saves the next operator the ~30 min I spent diagnosing.
  - **Success**: `docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` exists with a section "`claude --print` fails with 'Prompt is too long'" containing: (a) symptom screenshot/text, (b) root cause explanation (auto-loaded context overflow), (c) workarounds (devin worker recommended path; `--bare` + API key alternative), (d) verification (`echo 'reply OK' | claude --print` should exit 0 with response "OK"). README.md "Troubleshooting" section links to this doc. `pnpm lint:md` (markdownlint) exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: If the doc adds confusion (operators try `--bare` without API key + report new "Not logged in" failures, OR they expect the doc to fix their setup automatically), trim the workarounds list to just the devin-worker recommendation and link upstream to anthropic-claude-code's docs for the auth detail. Doc is reference, not a tool.
